when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她確實做了一些 , 但 , 真正的是 , 說未來會比這個還要多 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 又發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器完全是機械的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全是理論上
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的角度來的 , 但圖靈告訴我們一些非常重要的事情 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 然後說: 「 不管你怎麼製造一台電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不論你的電腦有沒有機械 , 就像babbage的機械 , 或是電子 , 就像現在的電腦一樣 , 或是在未來 , 細胞 , 或者 , 再一次 , 機械 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 把它做得很小 , 所有這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上 , 有一個計算本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這被稱為教堂的論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage已經建立了一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它有能力用電腦來做今天我們做的一切 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓大家知道它有多緩慢 , 大約有1k的記憶 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用了打孔卡 , 被進去了 , 它跑了大約一萬倍 , 第一輛zx81 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個拉姆派克 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加上額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 今天這會帶給我們什麼呢 ?
so there are plans .	所以有了計劃 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館檔案庫中 , 有數以百計的計劃和數以千計的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴貝奇所寫 , 關於這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一組是我們稱之為 「 計畫28 」 的計畫 , 也是我從多倫斯卡德開始的慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的電腦運算員 , 也是那個驅動計畫建立改變引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部這裡 , 我們將建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個計劃有幾個部分
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	一個是掃描babbage的檔案 。
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	那已經完成了 。 第二 , 現在正是研究那些計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三個部分是那台機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館實體建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造出來時 , 你終於能夠理解一個電腦是如何運作的 , 因為 , 與其在你面前有一個小小的晶片 , 你必須看著這個擁抱的東西 , 說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體操作 , 我看到cpu運作 , 我聽到它運作 。 我可能聞起來 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫的 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它肯定會引導未來科學的發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有蓋過它 , 因為他總是帶著新的計畫 , 但當它確實建在1940年代時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我給你一點口味 , 看看它在動作中看起來是什麼樣子 , 影片中只有cpu機制的一部分在運作 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 還會加起來 。 這是加入機制 , 所以你想像一下這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年的時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代發生之前 , 我們會有
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像的演講中 , 雅南•亞瑟伯特蘭將他三個最近期的項目展示在人類和我們的棲息地上 , 在他的系列《地球》中 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 在他的網頁專案《六十億人》中 , 他的 「 家園 」 , 透過呼吸影片 , 記錄人類對環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、電影、未來、人性、媒體、攝影、攝影等 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarthhusbertrand在廣角度捕捉到脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 要靠飛機來這裡旅行 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態 , 我一年內排放的二氧化碳就跟法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼做呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我得在回家時殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來做我的碳定位 , 就像我每次做的事一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是展現我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 是我去年拍的最後一張照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯塔沙油 , 很多污染物
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	要知道問題 ; 我們不想相信我們所知道的事 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在alberta人民工作的非op , 24小時到7小時 , 盡其所能地提煉石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的末端
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	石油沙並不是一個長期的解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量比我們每年發現的多出三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新加利多尼亞的珊瑚礁
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	百分之百的珊瑚可能在2050年之前就被丟棄 , 因為全球暖化 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	而且你知道珊瑚對溫度有多敏感 , 對海洋的生物多樣性來說是非常重要的 。

now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在大西洋和太平洋之間有了新的開拓方式 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	北極的厚度從1960年就減少了超過40% 。

it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了它80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家 , 在一百年內所有的山冰會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命是非常重要的 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾告訴你的 , 有20億人住在喜馬拉雅冰河的水上 。

these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物 , 幾億年的歷史 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	而我們人類已經直立行走了20萬年 。

for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	數世代以來 , 我們一直在養育我們的孩子 , 不像其他數百萬的物種生活在我們身邊 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去三十年來 , 我已經密切地看著地球和它的dwellers , 來自天空中高處 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生命與地球的福祉綁在一起 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、養殖 , 至今仍是世界上最重要的人類佔領 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	而把我們結合在一起的 , 遠遠大於我們分裂的事物 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都對地球的禮物有相同的需求 , 希望能在自身上升 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而我們卻在養育牆壁上繼續拆開 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	現今 , 我們最大的戰役是要保護我們星球的自然提供 。

half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失了 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的運作率很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	密集的耕種正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源並不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們自己瀕臨絕種 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只在努力改善生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但財富差距卻越來越廣 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們尚未明白 , 我們要走的速度比地球還快 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 現今的解決方案是可行的 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的演講中 , richardresnick指出 , 基因定序即將把醫療照護顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、衛生保健、科學、科技、科技
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷尼克:歡迎來到基因體革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給你們看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大x染色體 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 還有y的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	抱歉男孩們 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你有所不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組 , 那麼你看到的當然就是這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼--拼出這四個生化字母 , 或者我們稱之為鹼基 , 沒錯:a、c、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億個 。
is that a big number ?	那是個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨意丟出大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這個1280年的每一個像素都放在1280年的每一個像素上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕 , 來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為它的大小 , 一群人 , 順便一提 , 有y染色體決定他們會想要定序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 其實15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組排序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本被出版了 , 他們一直在努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都在一台看起來像這樣子的機器上完成 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本大約是一美元--一個很慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴你們 , 這個世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以現在我們要做的是把一個基因組做成50個複製品 , 我們把所有的複製品都切成50個鹼基的讀法 , 然後我們將它們定序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這些帶到軟體裡 , 重新組合起來 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	所以 , 給各位看一下這個樣子 , 人類的基因組計畫:3gbs , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器在一週內執行:200gabes 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	那200人將在今年夏天改變到600年 , 沒有這個步調緩慢的跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 一個基地的價格 , 來定序一個基地 , 已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	那就等同於你在1998年把車蓋滿了氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星和後面兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、定位、所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、舊式定序的方式 , 這裡是全新的東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是個標誌尺度 , 你們通常不會看到像那樣的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以 , 今年全球人類基因組排序的能力大約有五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而我們根據被放置的機器而知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	這是預期未來的兩倍、三倍 , 或四倍的一年 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 特別有一間實驗室 , 代表了那能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對能贏得這場新月球的比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有什麼意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人是37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她用 「 階段二型雌激素接收性乳癌 」 來呈現 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她帶著三種c型卵巢癌的階段回來 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時回來 , 患有更多卵巢癌、更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著急性髓性白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 死於八天後 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士被對待的方式 , 只有十年的時間 , 看起來會像血流一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	而是因為像我同事rickwilson這樣的人 , 在華盛頓大學的基因研究所 , 她決定去看這位女士的後期 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他做了序列 , 拿皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 和癌症骨髓 , 他在兩個禮拜內完成完整的基因組排序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他把這兩個基因組在軟體中做比較 , 他發現 , 在其它東西當中 , 是一個刪除2000個核酸 , 橫跨300億個鹼基的特定基因 , 叫做tp53 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因中有這種敏捷的突變 , 你一生中有90%的機率會得到癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這並不能幫助這位女士 , 但如果你願意的話 , 對她的家人的影響會很嚴重 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們會得到這個基因測試 , 然後他們會了解 , 那麼他們就可以去取得普通的螢幕 , 並且他們可以在早期捕到癌症 , 有可能活得更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我向各位介紹啤酒雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時就診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的媽媽是一位非常勇敢的女人 , 她不相信症狀不符合 , 透過一些英勇的努力和許多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的 , 是預防性的失明症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了dopa , 他們的症狀確實改善了 , 但他們沒有完全不符合症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果這張照片裡的先生是一位名叫joebeery的傢伙 , 他很幸運能成為一家叫生命科技的公司的樂團 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家公司之一 , 使得這些大規模的基因組定序工具 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以 , 他做的是讓孩子們有序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 在一個叫做spr的基因中 , 有一系列突變 , 它負責製造出血清素 , 其他東西 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在奧巴的頂端 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素先驅藥物 , 他們現在的效果很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 這絕對不會發生 , 沒有完整的基因序列 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	而在幾年前 , 這要花十萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬美元 。 明年是一千美元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在它100美元後的一年 , 給或一年後 ,
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是這移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有小小的尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和戒槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 腹部像飢荒受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道基本上會打開 , 糞便就會流入他的腸道中 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以 , 一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我祈禱 。 我在這麼多的痛苦中 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好在臨床遺傳學上有一個背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子的基因組定序吧 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現 , 在一個控制細胞死亡的基因中 , 一個單一的突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以 , 理論是 , 他對於食物本質上發生的事 , 會有免疫反應 , 那是自然的反應 , 造成了一些已編程的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但調節下面的基因卻破碎了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也是一種治療骨髓移植的治療方法 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的磨練復原後 , 他現在用a1醬汁吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	把基因組當成一個普遍診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們身上了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對我們所有人來說 , 這代表的是 , 在座的每個人 , 可以多過五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想到人類在地球上的足跡 , 以及我們維持糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的科技也被用來種植玉米、小麥、黃豆和其他農作物 , 那些高容忍乾旱、洪水、害蟲 , 以及殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在看 , 只要我們持續增加人口數 , 我們就得要繼續成長、吃基因改造的食物 , 那是我今天要採用的唯一立場 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非觀眾中有任何人想要自願不再吃飯 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 不是一個 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來每台桌面都一躍 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上被這個東西刪除了 。
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	接著 , 更一般的字流處理器出現了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但最終 , 卻在顛覆的頂端上造成了顛覆 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	那是bobmecalfe發明了ethernet和所有這些電腦的連結從根本上改變了一切
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間我們有了netscape , 我們有了yahoo , 整個網路泡沫化了 。

so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	所以我最近只需要買生活保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我需要回答:a 。 我從來沒有做過基因檢測 , b 。 我這裡有一位 , c 。 我有一個 , 我沒有說 。
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我能夠回答a , 我說老實說 , 以防我的人生保險經紀人在傾聽 。

consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者對基因組學的應用 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。

so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以 , 今天在場的任何人 , 都帶著你顯著的另外一個人 , 轉向他們 , 張開嘴巴 , 送到實驗室 , 然後你肯定知道 。

and it looks really good .	而且看起來真的很好 。

how many people in the audience have the last name resnick like me ? raise your hand .	觀眾中有多少人有像我一樣的姓氏resnick ? 請舉手 。

so my father's father was one of 10 resnick brothers .	所以我父親的父親是十位雷尼克兄弟中的一個 。
they all hated each other .	他們都討厭彼此 。

but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但想像一下 , 如果我的基因組被定位了 , 坐在軟體裡 , 第三表兄的基因組也坐在那兒 , 也有軟體可以比較這兩個 , 做出這些聯想 。
not hard to imagine . my company has software that does this right now .	不難想像 。 我的公司有這樣的軟體 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	danielkraftdemos他的骨髓礦物質一個新裝置 , 它很快就收集了救命的骨髓 , 帶著最小的痛苦到捐贈者 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中找到的成年幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多臨終條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物、生物科技、衛生保健、醫學、科學、科技、科技、
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了更好的方式來收割骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	所以我是一位小兒科癌症醫師 , 也是史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床焦點一直是骨髓移植術 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor得到啟發 , 我沒有帶一個人的大腦 , 但我確實帶了一升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的性命 , 大部分患有先進的惡性惡性惡性 , 例如白血病和淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做我的移植計畫 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國來拯救白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 一般的麻醉 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生 , 來自我 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌上 , 我們拿著這種小針頭 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	我們這樣做的方式基本上就是透過軟組織來定位 , 將它打到硬骨中 , 進入tuchus這個技術名詞 , 並激發大約十個骨髓的磁鐵 , 每次都有針筒 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後將它交給護士 , 她將它丟到一個錫罐裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	將它交回給我 。 我們一而再再而三地這麼做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百倍通常
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我的手臂的結尾是sore , 我手上有一通電話 , 更不用說bob , 他的結尾看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在40年內都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	這樣做可能有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到一個微創入侵的方法 , 一個我們稱之為 " 骨髓礦工 " 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓礦工 , 它的運作方式就在這裡展現 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準鋸齒患者
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只進入一次 , 進入臀部或臀部的前面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性、有力的導管 , 有一個特殊的電線迴圈尖端 , 會停留在骨髓的殘留部位內 , 跟隨著臀部的輪廓 , 隨著它移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它能讓你非常快速的抱負 , 或快速的吸出 , 豐富的骨髓 , 透過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過同樣的入口 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能得到一個穿刺 , 當地的麻醉 , 把這個收起來當成一個病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛拿到一個小型的捐贈品 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩種大型動物 , 豬的研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不只拿到骨髓 , 還拿到骨髓中的幹細胞活動十倍 , 和正常裝置相比 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才剛剛fda核准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這裡是活生生的病人 , 你可以看到它跟著彈性曲線在附近 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這裡會有兩個通過 , 在同一個病人身上 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在當地麻醉藥品下做的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	我們又得到了 , 比起同一個病人所做的標準方法多了3到6倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是成體幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很棒的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞在我們體內 , 包括我們骨髓中的血液幹細胞 , 這種幹細胞已經被我們用作一種幹細胞療法 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年裡 , 骨髓幹細胞爆發了一種爆炸 , 來治療病人的其他疾病 , 像是心臟病、血管疾病、血管疾病、組織工程 , 甚至在神經學上 , 用來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出來 , 商業化 , 今年 , 世代2.0的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望這能得到更多幹細胞 , 轉譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人簽名 , 成為拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	它甚至可能可以讓你銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你年輕時、更健康時 , 在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植倖存者 , 他們每年在史丹佛聚集在一起 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi對宇宙有爭議性的新模型 , 可能只能回答所有大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西 , 它是最美麗的基本粒子的8維空間模型 , 強迫你看過的 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi理論在他的一切理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些殺手方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能去描述粒子物理的美好 , 不用方程式來描述 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚頭都由數千個聚合物組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些聚苯乙烯酸酯會持續繁殖和分支 , 成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是個超智能的珊瑚 , 我們就能單獨的一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點 , 和他的鄰居相比 , 如果只是機會 , 或命運 , 或命運 , 又怎樣 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 在慶祝我們把溫度調高到太高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是笨蛋 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是很類似的意思 , 你看 , 我有衝浪疤來證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這個聚合物會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居顯然是他一模一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 但經歷他們是獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	不像我們 , 一個超級智慧的珊瑚會獨特的準備去了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述我們的宇宙運作方式 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們我們的現實是持續分支到不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是一件奇怪的事 , 可以包容我們的心靈 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子怪異最早被厄爾丁•薛丁格和他的貓描述 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓喜歡這個版本更好
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設置中 , 薛丁格在一個有放射性樣本的箱子中 , 由量子力學定律所組成 , 分支成一個狀態 , 一個放射線和一個沒有的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本輻射的分支中 , 它會造成觸發 , 釋放出毒藥和薛丁格已死 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實是被每個個體分開來的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	要不就是說 , 要不然 , 另一個就不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只經歷一個個別的存在 , 而我們不見到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每個人 , 像薛丁格在這裡 , 都是一種珊瑚分支 , 進入不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這是世界在微小的尺度下運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	它可以以單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的一切 , 確實 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不意味著一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其餘的物理則是要描述哪些可能發生 , 以及哪些不能 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們的是 , 一切都歸功於幾何學 , 以及基本粒子的交互作用 。
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	唯有這些互動是完全平衡的 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的了解 , 它們是什麽 , 以及這個平衡是如何運作的 。
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子的光束會加速到接近光速 , 並在撞擊中聚集在一起 , 產生出一股純能量的爆炸 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這個能量立刻被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 上面有偵測器和電腦 , 用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器--日內瓦的大型強子對撞機--有十七英里--當它在運作時 , 比蒙特瑞市還要多五倍的權力 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測哪些粒子會在任何個別碰撞中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性都意識到
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理的確告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量一定跟質子和反質子的質量一樣 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量限制還大的粒子 , 都沒有產生出來 , 而且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器如此令人興奮的原因 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將推動這個能量限制七倍以外的能量因此我們很快就會看到一些新粒子
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到的事物之前 , 讓我來描述我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大多數人都熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的許多人 , 都讓他們過得不錯 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴 , 叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷和一個很小的質量 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 最上下的夸克有非常大的質量 , 並且在三分之一中結合 , 讓原子內部的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子都出現在左邊和右邊的品種中 , 都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代 , 它的載荷和第一代相同 , 但有更高的質量 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都與各種力粒子互動 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力與電荷相互作用透過稱為光子的粒子傳導物質
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	也有一種很弱的力量 , 叫做 , 很不想像 , 很弱的力量 , 只會和左撇子互動 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	強力在夸克間作用 , 帶有不同種類的載荷 , 稱為顏色荷 , 三種不同的品種:紅、綠和藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygellmann為這些名字-他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 有重力的力量 , 它透過質量和旋轉來互動 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	這裡最要了解的是 , 每種力量都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量與物質相互作用 , 根據每個粒子所擁有的相對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 它給所有其他粒子帶來質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到這個希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎確定它會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最棒的奧秘是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示一個美麗的可能性 , 來到這場演講的結尾 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用它們的旋轉和載荷來計算這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226個 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	那是很多的粒子可以持續追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	似乎很奇怪 , 大自然會有這麼多基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據它們的載荷來繪製它們 , 有些美麗的圖案會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 一個負電荷 , 夸克有三分之一的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以 , 當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子 , 它的電荷總和一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子也有反粒子 , 相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現電荷其實是另外兩個電荷的組合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們將超荷和弱荷散播出去 , 將粒子的載荷標示在這個二度載荷空間中 , 電荷就在這些粒子沿著垂直方向坐在那裡 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力與物質相互作用 , 根據它們的超荷和弱荷相互作用 , 這會使得這個圖案 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這被稱為 「 統一式電擊模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	大部份人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這兩種都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊這裡的希格斯有很大的質量 , 打破這種電擊模式的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它使弱力變得非常微弱 , 通過給弱粒子一個大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	既然這個巨大的希格斯坐在橫向圖中 , 電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量 , 並在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以 , 電磁力和弱力被二維空間中的粒子載荷所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力的力量透過它的兩個載荷方向傳遞出去 , 將夸克中的力粒子的載荷沿著這些方向移動 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四維的載荷空間中被繪製出來 , 投射到像這樣的二維空間中 , 讓我們能看到它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子互動時 , 大自然就會把東西保持在一個完美的平衡 , 沿著這四個載荷方向 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和一個反粒子碰撞 , 它會在四個載荷方向中產生一股能量和一個總負荷的能量 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以創造出來 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 並且維持為零的總載荷 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	例如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 負荷必須要永遠保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個微弱的粒子可以腐化成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個仍然是零總載荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些負荷的模式並不只是漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們哪些互動是被允許發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以以四度空間旋轉這個載荷空間 , 來更好地觀察強度的交互作用 , 它有這個很好的六角形對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強烈的互動中 , 一個強力粒子 , 例如這一個 , 和一個有色夸克互動 , 例如這個綠色的夸克 , 用不同的顏色來掌控這個紅色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強烈的互動 , 每秒鐘發生數百萬次 , 在我們體內的每一個原子核中 , 把原子核黏在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四種指控對應三種力量並不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們也可以將兩個載荷與重力相對應 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們納入這些時 , 每個物質粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中給一個好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看看它相當漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個模式符合我們目前最棒的知識 , 關於大自然是如何在這些基本粒子的微小尺度下建立的 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們肯定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子在實驗上是極限的 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道這些微小的尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小的尺度運作的方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要討論一些關於我們還不知道的事情的新舊想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否把手放在整個尼古拉達 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到所有製造我們宇宙的粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測當實驗達到更高能量時 , 我們會看到的新粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 就是這個已知的載荷模式 , 不太對稱 , 可以從一個更完美的圖案中浮現出來 , 和希格斯粒子如何破解電磁圖案 , 來賦予電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向引進新的力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們介紹一個新的方向時 , 我們會猜測粒子沿著這個方向的載荷是什麼 , 然後我們可以與他人一起旋轉它 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷中建構出標準載荷的指數 , 作為一個在七度載荷維度中更完美的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個特別的選擇對應於1973年巴蒂和薩拉姆的一個統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的統一模式時 , 我們可以看到粒子似乎缺少了幾個缺口 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論運作的方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	一個物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 將被建立的圖案視為次等 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 該粒子的存在應該很像弱力 , 只有弱力 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組載荷 , 考慮到關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:物質的第二代和第三代在六度載荷空間中有完全相同的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並不是獨一無二的被它們的六個載荷分辨出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間的上方 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以分配每個粒子的獨特新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們就可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個模式會是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到第二代和第三代物質的關係 , 現在是第一代的對稱性 , 叫做 「 試驗性 」 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種特殊的載荷模式在八度空間中實際上是數學中最美麗的幾何結構的一部分 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	它是最大的例外謊言團體的模式 , e8 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是平滑的 , 彎曲的形狀有248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	這個圖案中的每一點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的一種對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	這個e8形狀的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦一般廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	和量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙在最小尺度下如何運作的一切 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的形狀 , 活在八度載荷空間中 , 是很美麗的 , 它能總結出上千種可能的交互作用 , 在這些基本粒子之間 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其它錯綜複雜的圖案包含在這個圖案中 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	用一個特別的旋轉 , 我們可以從這個圖案中看出 , 沿著一個對稱軸 , 同時看到所有粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 在那裡 , 新粒子是由這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	這裡有20個缺口 , 新粒子應該是 , 其中兩個已經被帕塔拉姆粒子填滿了 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置在這個圖案中 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的擴展場 , 但有顏色充電 , 和強力互動 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子中 , 完成了這個模式 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是個很棒的前景 , 這個偉大數學美的物體可以用最小尺度來描述粒子互動的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而大自然被數學描述的這個想法並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫下這句話: 「 大自然的宏偉書一直開放給我們的凝視 , 是用數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形 , 沒有它是人類不可能理解的單一字詞 ; 沒有這些 , 一個在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾試著遵循伽利略的指引 , 用只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何圖形來描述粒子物理學的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的在研究這些東西時 , 數學可以像一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但 , 放心的是 , 在這個數學的核心是純潔的 , 美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入量子力學 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在各個位置互動 , 根據一個漂亮的圖案 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著更多的圖案出現 , 利用像大型強子對撞機的新機器 , 我們也許能看到大自然是否使用這個e8圖案 , 或不一樣的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一項很棒的探險 , 要參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc找到符合這個e8模式的粒子 , 那會非常非常酷 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果lhc找到新粒子 , 但它們不符合這個模式 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對這個e8理論卻不利 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟呢 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 相當糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然是如何運作的 , 是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部分這些點子可能不會成為自然界的真相 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣:有很多野生動物 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	以任何大型投資來說 , 若沒有實現 , 若要放棄一系列的研究 , 可能會有情感上的困難 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有東西沒用 , 你就得把它丟出去 , 試試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在 , 要維持清潔和成就快樂的唯一方式 , 在這種不確定性中 , 就是保持平衡和觀點 , 在人生中保持平衡 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪中平衡我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	如此一來 , 就算我所從事的物理 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	而我試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年 , 我大部分時間都住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美麗的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是宇宙中最棒的謎團之一 , 讓我父母了解我如何在沒有全職工作的情況下存活下來 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我會讓你進到那個秘密中 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊的家裡辦公室的景象 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景觀很相似 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾經是我在毛伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我曾經選擇過非常不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心租金讓我花時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	生活在遊牧的存在 , 時常很難過 , 但這讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 保持平衡 , 在我的生活中 , 我一直很高興 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間與超智能珊瑚掛在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能在這裡受邀來ted
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概了解其中的百分之二 , 但我仍然很喜歡 。 所以 , 我要聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你對一切的理論-garretlisi:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克里斯:沒錯 。 它之所以會讓少數人感到興奮 , 是因為 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是說 , 我們應該把宇宙想成 , 在它的心中 , 最小的東西 , 是不是可能的e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 是否在最小尺度上有這樣的尺度 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	蓋爾:嗯 , 現在我給你看的圖案是對應到我們所知的基本粒子物理學已經對應到一個非常美麗的形狀
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀有著驚人的相似性 , 以及它符合這張e8圖案的方式 , 可能是圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我展示給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 其實代表了我們經歷的高維物體的對稱性 , 會在我們經歷的時空中移動、跳舞和跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但是 , 弦理論學家 , 如我所知 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待電子與e8有關聯 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	蓋爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 隨著時空移動的形狀 , 它會扭曲 。 隨著它移動的方向 , 就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	大了嗎 ? 小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	蓋爾:嗯 , 就我們所知 , 電子就是點粒子 , 所以這會降到最小可能的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 這些東西在量子場理論中被解釋的方式是 , 所有的可能性都會同時擴大和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會用類比來做珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8所使用的方式就是 , 每一次在時空中 , 都會附著一個形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說 , 形狀會扭曲這個方向 , 形狀會扭曲 , 隨著曲線的表面移動 , 正是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 它們表現出自己是指點 , 這樣互動的方式 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我是否能把這弄得更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克里斯:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	這引發了一種神奇的感覺 , 我當然想更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你來 。 這絕對令人著迷 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古拉爾談到塔卡爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 協助在波普非洲城鎮中的人 , 和受到威脅的動物生活在旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古拉爾幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 不管怎樣 ,
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 賈博 , 古博 , 古博 , 布恩索爾 , 但我們也可以 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所發出的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊傳到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一個 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想用我的演說來談談昨天的斑拉留下的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他在談論這個了不起、三歲的澳洲孩童賽拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過歷史、家譜樹 , 透過dna的遺傳資料 , 人類是人類的 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是古生物學家 , 路易斯•李克 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	那時還蠻不尋常的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	這有點常見 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺跡 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	而你能分辨很多關於那些從化石看來的樣子 , 從肌肉附著的形狀 , 從各式各樣的人造物中發現的 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們行為如何呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張且現在是相當普遍的理論 , 如果我們在我們最接近的生物親戚身上找到行為模式 , 或相同的理論 , 現今的人類 , 那麼 , 也許那些行為在七百萬年前就出現在人猿、人類的祖先身上 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們將這些特質帶給我們從古代、古代的歷史 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看看現今處理人類演化的教科書 , 你通常會發現人們推測人類早期的行為 , 根據黑猩猩的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	它們比任何其他活生生的生物都更像我們 , 我們在ted大會上也聽說過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 這對我來說 , 對於黑猩猩和我們很像 , 對於牠們行為的某些面向來說 , 它仍然會留下評論 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給了他們名字 。 他們可以活到六十年或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部分的人可能不會在野外賺到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 雌性先生在11或12歲時 , 生下了她的第一個嬰兒 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她每五六年只有一個嬰兒 , 一個長期的童年依賴兒童 , 當孩子在晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 然後騎在她背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	而我們相信這長期的童年對黑猩猩來說是很重要的 , 就像對我們來說 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在演化過程中變得更加複雜 , 在不同形式的動物中 , 我們發現 , 學習在個體的生命歷史中扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	而年輕的黑猩猩花了很多時間看他們的長老們做的事 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道他們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 用這種方式 , 讓現在在所有不同黑猩猩族群中看到的不同工具行為 , 在非洲 , 研究這些行為如何從一代傳到下一代 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 如此一來 , 我們就能把這些工具行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語 , 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們的確有很豐富的姿勢和手勢 , 很多都很相似 , 甚至和我們一模一樣 , 在相同的情境中形成 。 迎接黑猩猩們擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	牠們也親吻 , 手 , 手 , 把另一隻放在後面 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們會搖擺 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩社會中 , 我們發現許多有同情心的例子 , 例如愛和真正的利他主義 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的天性有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力極度殘忍 , 甚至是一場原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具侵略性的行為 , 最多的部分是指導鄰近社會群體的個體 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	它們非常有侵略性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比起其他任何生物 , 已經幫助我們了解 , 畢竟人類和動物王國之間沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨時愈來愈模糊 , 當我們觀察到更多 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍持續進行著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外 , 過著複雜的社會生活 , 比起其他任何事情 , 都更能幫助我們意識到我們是其中的一部分 , 和我們共享地球的驚人動物不分開 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到黑猩猩是很可悲的 , 就像世界上許多其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它讓你看到gombe的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	就在我飛過整個區域的時候 , 大約16年前 , 我發現 , 在公園外 , 這片森林 , 1960年 , 在塔肯尼卡湖東邊的海岸上 , 幾乎沒有被打破 , 就是那個小的、30平方的戈姆布國家公園 , 那個問題來到我腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何甚至能試著拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的居民 , 卻在掙扎著求生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	居住的人口比土地還多 , 可能還能支持 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量會增加 , 從布朗伊州湧入 , 以及從剛果湖進來的 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人他們買不起其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個程式 , 我們稱之為塔卡爾 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種非常全面的方式來改善生活在公園附近的村莊裡的人 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	它從12個村莊開始 , 現在是24個 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探討 , 但它包含了像是樹木護理 , 養殖方法現在最適合這一點 , 幾乎像沙漠般的土地在這些山區 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制的方式 , 防止土壤侵蝕
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新利用過度使用的農田的方式 , 這樣在兩年內就能再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井中取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建立了一些教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與小組女性合作 , 提供她們微額貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	而且 , 如同全世界的情況一樣 , 大約有95%的貸款歸還 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性權力 , 與教育一起工作 , 提供獎學金給女孩子們 , 讓他們能完成中學 , 在清晰的了解中 , 全世界的女性教育都能改善 , 家庭規模下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫的結果 , 有些事情發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育狀況是 , 住在這24個村莊裡的農夫 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順帶一提 , 許多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始塔卡爾計畫時 , 是一個坦尚尼亞人的團隊進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞團隊和村民談話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育有興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 隨著他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更加了解保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 身為山丘的上層是樹木的下層 , 所以你有了這可怕的土壤侵蝕和泥沼 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發我們所謂的更大的gombe生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是國家公園之外的一個區域 , 延伸到所有這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	隨著這些村莊有更好的生活標準 , 他們其實同意把10%到20%的土地放在高地的一旁 , 這樣一來 , 隨著樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩就會有葉廊 , 通過它們可以到達與國家公園以外的其他遺傳小組相互作用 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 塔卡爾是個成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方也在其他地方複製 , 圍繞著其他的荒野地區 , 面臨極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 如同我們在ted的前幾天討論的問題 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有一大堆的貧窮
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	而當你得到大量住在土地上的居民 , 不是那麼肥沃 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 把土壤留給侵蝕的機會 , 如同絕望的族群 , 砍掉更多的樹木 , 這樣他們就可以試著為自己和家人種植食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 有些事必須給予 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他的問題 , 不僅僅是非洲 , 還有開發中國家的其他國家 , 確實 , 無論我們在地球上都在做些什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家e.o.wilson說如果地球上的每一個人都能確保生活在歐洲或美國的平均水準我們就需要三個新星球
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但是我們沒有它們 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們是這樣的 , 可說是走過地球的最聰明的人 , 擁有這種非凡的頭腦 , 能夠說明的科技是如此地被這些ted會議所描述 , 然而我們卻破壞了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決定之前 , 曾經圍坐著問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大決策──我在這裡不特別談到非洲 , 但已開發國家的重大決策 , 包括數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是基於 「 這會如何影響下一個股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響到非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始到非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林時 , 我了解到越來越多非洲的問題 , 可能在之前殖民時代剝削的門口躺著 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲外旅行 , 在歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 去亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	而且你知道我在說的那種 。 我指的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水也許是這世紀我們將面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都是水被農業、工業和家庭化學物污染 , 至今仍在世界各地被噴灑 , 似乎無法從過去經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 ; 像是海嘯的效應越來越嚴重 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經討論過土壤的侵蝕
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無縫的燃燒化石燃料和其他溫室氣體的燃燒 , 所以就叫氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 世界各地 , 人們開始相信氣候有問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候都混雜起來 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是受影響較差的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	已經受到影響的非洲
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱的狀況就更糟了 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨雨來臨時 , 通常會導致洪水和增加苦惱 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	而居住的居民數目是土地無法支援的 , 他們太貧窮了 , 無法購買食物 , 他們不能搬走 , 因為整片土地已經退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以你會得到沙漠化 , 令人毛骨悚然 , 隨著樹木的最後一片被砍掉 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	而這種東西不只在非洲 , 全世界都如此 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到了好多年輕人 , 他們似乎失去了希望 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎已經失去了智慧 , 原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 各位認為 , 在這種非凡聰明的大腦之間 , 可能有某種不相干的斷層 , ted科技所表現出的那種大腦 , 以及人類的心 ? 用非科學的角度來談它 , 在愛和同情之間 。 是否有一些不相干的連結 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上 , 他們不是憂鬱或冷淡 , 或痛苦 , 和生氣 。 他們說的都是一樣的 。 他們說: 「 我們會這樣感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 沒有任何我們能做的 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們 , 我想我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 自從我是他們的年紀以來 , 我感受到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	導致這個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽 , 它從坦尚尼亞開始 , 現在已經傳播到全世界的97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	是象徵性的 。 根會製造出堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	槍聲看似微不足道 ; 為了抵達太陽它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成我們在地球上遇到的所有問題、環境和社交問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人 , 都能突破 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的訊息:我們每一個人每一天都會有所不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有一個選擇 。 在座的每一個人 , 我們都能選擇我們想要做什麼樣的不同 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人沒有選擇 , 我們要改變事情 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體全都選擇了三個項目
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們有多老 , 哪個國家 , 不論他們在城市或鄉下 , 都取決於什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始自己的根源和芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一組人都選擇 , 在他們之間 , 三種不同的項目 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 認識到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一個計畫將是幫助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們可能會募集資金來幫助世界其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一項計畫是幫助動物 , 不只是野生動物 , 馴獸動物也一樣 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	而他們的其中一個計畫將是幫助我們共同的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	整體來說 , 要學習和平和和諧 , 要在我們自己、家庭、社區、國家、文化、宗教之間 , 和我們之間的和平共存 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然界 。 我們不能以我們現在的速度去破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們的確沒有比這個星球還多 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	剛剛在非洲這裡挑出一兩個項目 , 根與芽的團體 , 只在坦尚尼亞 , 烏干達 , 肯亞 , 南非 , 剛果巴拉扎維爾 , 獅子山共和國 , 喀麥隆和其他團體 。 正如我所說的 , 在世界上的九十七個國家裡 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 和雞一起賣雞蛋 , 為了一點錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽家人 , 感受到一種自豪和賦權的感覺 , 因為他們不再對他人無助 , 取決於他們的蔬菜和雞 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予一些心理上的幫助 , 給予士兵們 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣的計畫 , 就是把他們自己帶出去 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會有用的成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時間了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要成分 , 年紀較大的孩子和年輕的孩子談話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而沒有預期的懷孕之類的 , 年輕人會從其他青年中傾聽更好 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 那是我在世界各地問的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多可怕的事情 , 你看過黑猩猩數目大約從一百萬分之一開始 , 在本世紀初 , 到現在沒有超過十五萬隻 , 和其他許多動物都一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 一旦有森林 , 沙漠就在那裡 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted一樣的研討會 , 也沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這個神奇的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我很高興能來到人們談論堆肥的latrines 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把這些水沖下躺梯 , 很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	然後討論再生能源絕望的重要性 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否關心地球為我們的孩子 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有小孩或孫子、姪女、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
