and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的精英 , 我們可以為此做點什麼 。 我們可以為我們每天生活的方式做出選擇 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買的東西 , 穿什麼
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	他或她長大後會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或不論是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 和人類的心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這正是ted對我們的幫助 , google幫助了我們 , esri幫助我們繪製gombe國家公園 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們連結起來 , 開始實現 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你已經聽過了 , 開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 看到我們必須有的改變 , 只要我們關心未來 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望自然的下一個原因是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以拿一個絕對被破壞的區域 , 用時間 , 或許有些幫助它可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而一個例子就是tacare計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴過你 , 看似死去的樹木木木木頭 , 如果你停止用火柴來駭進它們 , 你不需要因為木頭很多 , 那麼五年內你就可以有一棵30呎長的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在滅絕的邊緣 , 可以給予第二次機會 。 那是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這真是鼓舞人心 。 這讓我來到我最後一個關於希望的類別 , 我們在過去的兩天中聽說過這一點:這個不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種對人類精神的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 以至於你認為會被貧窮或疾病給打擊的人 , 或其他的 , 可以自拔 , 有時用手 , 拿走他們社會的一部分 , 把他們改變世界的一部分 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看 , 非洲外有一兩個人真的很激勵人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但顯然納爾遜•曼德拉 , 從十七年辛苦的實體勞動中浮現出來 , 23年的囚禁中 , 有了這種神奇的寬恕能力 , 讓他能帶領他國家走出種族隔離的邪惡政權 , 卻沒有血保 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	住在奈及利亞的肯薩羅威 , 他接管了巨大的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都盡了全力 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是如此的鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人是年輕非洲人需要的榜樣 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也聽過其中的一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我真的很感激這個機會 , 再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人能聚在一起 , 談論這些事情 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	在那位年輕女子經營這整個會議中心的最後一個字 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她對她的認證感到非常興奮 。 她是根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導中
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這協助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 我非常非常興奮 , 能見到她 , 看到年輕人的其中一個例子 , 當他們被賦予權力 , 給予有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜柯恩分享了一些艱難的事實 , 關於海洋中的塑膠污染 , 以及我們的生活 , 以及一些思想 , 關於如何從塑膠垃圾漩渦中解放自己 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、使命的藍、海洋、塑膠等 ,
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我和塑膠袋一起工作 , 我把塑膠袋剪起來 , 再縫回來 , 作為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 過去二十年來 ,
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二、三維的碎片和雕塑 , 以及裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	與塑膠一起工作 , 大約八年後 , 我的一些作品開始裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	和我們一樣是平默的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在我進一步教育我自己關於塑膠的過程中 , 我其實意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成更小的位元 , 因為它總是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	而我們發現 , 很多在海洋環境中
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	過去幾年 , 我學會了太平洋垃圾堆和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我的初步反應和我認為這有很多人對學習的第一反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須去外面清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我實際上開發了一個提案 , 要用貨船出去 , 和兩艘分解的捕魚拖網 , 一台吊車 , 一台晶片機 , 和一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖是要走到健身房 , 提高對這個議題的意識 , 並開始把塑膠拿起來 , 把它放進一點點 , 冷的模塊中 , 讓它能被用來當作被開發的社區裡的建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和那些真的去過健身房的人談話 , 去研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 並且去做 , 我了解到 , 實際上 , 清潔它會在桶子裡的一小滴 , 相對於全世界每天產生多少東西 , 實際上 , 我需要回頭來 , 看著更大的圖片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的圖片是:我們需要找到一個可以關掉水龍頭的方法 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們得要把單一use和丟棄塑膠的污點剪掉 , 每天都要以全球的規模進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著那個 , 我也了解到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠 , 你還想想像在太平洋洋的中央 , 我學到現在有11個垃圾漩渦 , 在世界上五個主要的海洋中有塑膠 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我不只關心塑膠的健身房 , 還有超市裡的塑膠垃圾 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都包在塑膠上 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都包在塑膠上 , 甚至在健康食物市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是塑膠和毒素從塑膠插入到我們體內 , 進入我們的身體 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他都在研究這個議題的人聚在一起 , 我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多我們正在努力的倡議 , 但其中的一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	一是:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋中有80%到90%都是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不稱它為它是什麼 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收每個人的書 , 以永續和綠化為主題 , 以回收的概念為主 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把某樣東西放進去 , 不用再想一次 。
what is the reality of that ?	究竟是怎麼一回事 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的深入探討 , 尤其是當涉及到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分都只會被降低 , 或被燒掉 , 或被運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它是被降級的 , 轉換成較少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以再次成為玻璃瓶 , 或可以再次使用塑膠瓶 , 絕不可以再成為塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大議題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們看著並要求大家思考的事情是 , 我們在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 的前面增加了第四個r , 也就是拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	每當可能 , 拒絕單一和可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是非常老舊的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在正在收集這些酷炫的畢氏型容器 , 用這些 , 而不是用來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人做一個服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易就拿起一瓶不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 忘了帶你的臭酒瓶 , 再裝滿水或過濾的水 , 和購買塑膠瓶的水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的各位說的話 , 我知道你們對這個議題了解很多 , 就是這在海洋中是個巨大的問題 , 但這是我們身為消費者所創造出來的問題 , 我們能解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對議題的意識 , 來解決這個問題 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 不論何時 , 要選擇單一塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把幹細胞的莖綁在海洋中 , 如此一來 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個來自pattiemaes在麻省理工學院的實驗室的示範 , 由pranavftry主導的 , 是ted的buzz , 這是個可穿戴的裝置 , 用一個投影機為深刻互動的方式鋪路 。 想像一下: 「 少數族群報告 」 接著一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	示範 , 設計 , 介面設計 , 科技 ,
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattiemaes和pranavm誤差分別為第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我對這個問題很有興趣 , 想知道我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 一種能讓我們無縫接觸、容易取得新陳代謝或資訊的感覺 , 可能存在於某處 , 能協助我們做出正確的決定 , 關於我們所要面對的一切 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	在座有些人可能會爭論 , 嗯 , 今天的手機已經不是這樣了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見到某個人 , 當然 , 這是最上層的網絡位置 , 你不握某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能暫時握住我的手機 , google搜尋你嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你去超市的時候 , 你站在那一大堆不同類型的衛生紙上 , 你不會拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 然後去一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的廁所論文中哪些是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們沒有很容易取得這些相關的資訊 , 可以協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定接下來要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組一直在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不需要需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止最成功的努力 , 這在過程中還是很有用的 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在就戴著裝置 , 我們已經將它拼湊起來 , 將它和架子的零件拼湊在一起 , 順便說一下 , 這時候只需花350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個攜帶式的 , 電池驅動的投影系統 , 上面有一面小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些零件在我口袋裡通訊到我的手機 , 它的功能是通訊和運算裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕拉夫•弗特里 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何表面 , 開始用他的手 , 和他前面投射的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤四種顯著的手指 ,
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他穿著你可能認得出來的簡單標記蓋 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個更時髦的版本 , 你也可以用不同顏色來畫你的指甲 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	基本上攝影機會追蹤這四根手指 , 辨識出他製作的任何手勢 , 例如 , 一個長灘的地圖 , 放大 , 等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出有代表性的手勢 , 例如 「 拍照 」 的手勢 , 然後拍下你面前的任何東西 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上 , 投射出他所拍攝的所有照片 , 透過它們 , 將它們整理起來 , 等等 , 再一次 , 使用所有自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 在座有些人很可能在兩年前就在現場 , 看到jeffhan或有些人可能會想: 「 嗯 , 這看起來不像微軟的表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手 , 等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 走到任何表面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西是可取得的 , 和這個投影資料互動的 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	裝置是完全可攜式的 , 可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 其中一個重要的差異是 , 它完全是移動式 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的差異是 , 在大量生產中 , 明天比現今的手機費用不多 , 且其實不算是更大的包裝看起來比我脖子上的這個版本還多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們其中一些人活在幻想中 , 像tomcruise在《少數民族報告》中一樣酷的湯姆克魯斯 , 之所以我們對這個裝置感到很興奮的原因是 , 它真的能作為這六感裝置的其中一個 , 讓你有相關的資訊在你面前 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以 , 我們看到帕拉夫進入超市 , 他在購物一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品--這個系統可以辨識出他拿起的產品 , 使用圖像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以請求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 這裡的這個選擇是一項特別好的選擇 , 給他的個人標準 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能想要用衛生紙 , 上面有最多白化的 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿到亞馬遜的評分 , 在書的封面上被投射出來 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們先前的講者 , 順便說一下 , 亞馬遜的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕拉夫把書本的頁面翻過來 , 接著 , 看到了關於書讀者評論的額外資訊 , 可能是他最喜歡的批評家等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他轉到某個特定的頁面 , 他會發現一個意義 , 一個我們朋友的專家 , 給他一些額外的資訊 , 關於那個頁面上的任何東西 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀它從來不需要過時的報紙
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你能得到你正在讀的事件的影片 , 說明你能得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是更有爭議的一個 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted和某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個字雲 , 標籤的字眼 , 和那個人的部落格和個人網頁相關的字眼 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機過去 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的飛行被延遲了 , 大門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道目前的情況 , 就如你手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以 , 這就是我們目前正在發展的第六感 , 可以讓我們無縫地取得這些相關的資訊 , 來了解我們可能遇到的事物 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕拉夫 , 真的 , 就像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確應該得到很多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去的三個月裡睡得太多 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	而他的女朋友也可能對他不太高興 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但現在還不夠完美 , 進步非常多 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 也許在另一十年內 , 我們會在這裡 , 用終極的第六感大腦植入 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有一個強而有力的友誼 , 生於無法想像的失落 。 rodriguez的兒子在世界貿易攻擊中被殺害 , 在2001年9月11日 ; elwafi的兒子zacariasmoussaui被定罪在那些攻擊中扮演一個角色 , 希望能找到和平 , 這兩個媽們已經漸漸了解並尊重彼此 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911癒合:找到寬恕、友情的母親們 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 我們現在卻覺得很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我的兒子在2001年9月11日的世貿中心
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否曾死去 , 直到36小時之後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治性的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家要用我們兒子的名字 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 然而 , 透過震驚 , 震驚 , 以及我們人生中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個禮拜後 , 當zacariasmoussaoui被指出六個陰謀來犯下恐怖主義 , 美國政府向他要求死刑 , 如果定罪的話 , 我和我的丈夫反對 , 公開場合 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些 , 以及透過人權團體 , 我們和其他幾個受害者的家人團結在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我看到媒體中的aicha , 在她兒子被指示出來時 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想在我強壯時遇到那個女人 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深處的悲慟 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或者我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者時 , 我得到了立即的同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控的是什麼時 , 她沒有得到那份同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。

i suffered a lot as a mother .	我身為母親的許多苦難 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。

my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。

i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以 , 這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 所以我的痛苦對其他女性來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有女人而言 , 所有給予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	由於我們是女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定是手工的 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是對我們、對我們女人、對我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我對抗暴力 , 對抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校和年輕的穆斯林女孩談話 , 讓他們不接受與她們的意志結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免她們像我一樣結婚、受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。

and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都是為了害怕另一個 , 但讓那一步 , 然後意識到: 「 嘿 , 這實在太難了 。

by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 既然我一直在說話 , 全世界有另外一萬三千人正在受痢疾之苦 。

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶 , 因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯的毀滅性新聞 , 在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的日子和數週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那真的困在我身上 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	然後 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風滑到美國的一邊 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這裡是第一個世界國家 , 讓我們看看他們能做什麼 。 」

however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 在少數幾個失敗的原型之後 , 我終於想到了這個 , 終於是救命之瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好了 , 現在為了科學的一點 ,
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifsaver之前 , 最好的手過濾器只能過濾到大約200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約有200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒則是大約25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	那肯定會穿過那200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifsaver濾水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 什麼都沒有穿過 。

it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	會持續6000公升 。

so let's look at the applications .	所以 , 我們來看看應用程式 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?

and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到難民營 , 來取得他們的安全飲用水 。

diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病的傳播 。 需要的資源更多 。

but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考方式 , 運送這些 , 人們可以留下來 。

now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 這並不需要自然災害才能成功 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊思維 , 國家基礎設施和管道工作 , 實在太貴了 。

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水 , 使用人造流程來做 , 咱們用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡拿起水 , 將水淡化 , 免費運送到那裡 , 將它丟到山上 , 河流 , 和溪流上 。

so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 處理水在使用時 , 母親和孩子們不再需要每天走四小時才能收集他們的水 。

to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	若要把這點放到情境中 , 英國政府每年花費約12億英鎊在外國援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在那裡 ?

so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	所以每年受苦的三百五十億人 , 每年死亡的兩百萬個孩子 , 將會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	padyabdown聲稱我們正生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力從未有過改變 。 在tedxbruss的演講中 , 他把他所看到的三個重大的全球轉變放大了 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有首詩是十九世紀末一位非常有名的英文詩人寫的 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 在邱吉爾的腦中迴盪著 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩寫著: 「 在夏天的ide山丘上 , 帶著溪流的水流 , 哈克我聽到了一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像夢中有聲響 , 遠遠又近 , 又低又低 , 在地球的道路上 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵遊行 , 很快就死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " shropshirelad " 由a.e.休斯曼所寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所理解的 , 你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽到的 , 是十九世紀漫長、炎熱、絲毫的夏天 , 來到一個接近地點 , 我們即將邁入歷史中那段可怕的時期之一 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期總是 , 各位先生女士 , 都伴隨著亂流 , 血流太常 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我對你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責了 , 如果你們願意 , 生活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當權力被建立起來時 , 權力的秩序開始改變 , 以及世界的新觀點 , 新勢力就開始形成了 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	今天我們很清楚地看到 , 幾乎總是很亂七八糟的時代 , 很困難的時光 , 很多時候都很血腥 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一下 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生的那段時間 , 那就是休斯曼的感覺來臨 , 邱吉爾也覺得 , 當權力從古老的國家通過 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋 , 到美國的新興勢力 , 美國的起源於美國 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在真空之中 , 曾經有過的歐洲強權在上個世紀扮演著兩場血腥的災難──第一部分和第二部分的兩場:兩個世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經將他們視為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更精確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一次 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一個是 , 前兩個是關於權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些我想要參考的新維度 , 現在從來沒有發生過這種事 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力的轉變 , 發生在全世界 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	而今日的情況是 , 在某種意義上 , 恐怖的原因是因為它從未發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經見識到希臘的力量轉移到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明時期發生的權力轉移 , 但我們看到一些稍微不同的東西 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	對於權力 , 不只是稍微從國家轉移到國內 。
it's also moving vertically .	也是垂直移動的 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今發生的狀況是 , 被制定的權力 , 被責任 , 被告知法律規則 , 在國家國家的制度中 , 現在已經遷移到極大的全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	權力全球化的全球化我們談到市場的全球化 , 但其實它是真正力量的全球化 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級 , 權力在哪裡被告知要對法律規則負責 , 在國際舞台上 , 它不是 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 現在的權力是:網路的力量 , 衛星廣播公司的權力 , 貨幣改變者的力量 , 這個巨大的金錢協會 , 現在流通了三十二倍 , 交易所必要的金額 , 它應該有資金來資金改變者 , 如果你喜歡的話 , 財務推測者的力量 , 將我們全都帶到我們的膝蓋最近 , 跨國企業的力量 , 往往往往往比起我國更大 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球空間中 , 主要是不受規範的 , 不受法律規範的主題 , 而人們可能不受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在那件衣服強大到一瞬間 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	總是適合那些擁有最強權的人在沒有限制的空間中操作 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早或之後 , 不受規範的空間空間不會受到法律規範 , 不只由你想要的國際貿易、網路 , 等等 。 還有一些你不希望國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的東西 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9•11事件的啟示是即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 無論如何 , 那些居住空間的人 , 都能在你最具代表性的城市中攻擊你即使是在你最明亮的九月大早上也是如此 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約有60%被拿來資助9/11的四百萬美金 , 實際上是通過雙胞胎塔的機構 , 9/11摧毀了 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間──質量旅行、網路、衛星廣播者的空間 , 來擺脫它們的毒藥 , 就是要破壞我們的系統 , 以及我們的方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 或遲早 , 歷史的規則是 , 權力要遵守的地方 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果是這樣 , 正如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一種現象就是權力的全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是將治理帶到全球 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們面前的幾十年將會是為了更大或更少的動亂 , 我們能做到那樣的目標:把治理帶到全球的空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是指設立一些全球民主機構 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	我自己的看法 , 順便說一下 , 女士們先生們 , 這種做法不太可能是透過產卵更多的聯合國機構來完成的 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種手段 , 可以合法化國際行動 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 當談到全球空間的治理時 , 我的猜測是這樣的 , 不會透過更多的聯合國機構來創造 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強而有力的聚集在一起 , 製造出基於約定的系統 , 以條約為基礎的協議 , 來管理那個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到足以包容即使是最強大的國家 , 美國 , 如果必要的話 , 也要考慮到 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	kyoto:在掙扎的過程中 , 開始創造一個以約定為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	g20:我們現在知道 , 我們得要把一個有能力將治理帶到金融空間的機構 , 給財務推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而這就是g20的所在 , 一個以約定為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等一下會再回來談 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的團結結結起來 , 以條約為基礎的機構制定規則 , 來填補那個治理空間 , 那麼 , 留下的弱點會發生什麼事 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這真是個大問題 , 我們只要一秒鐘就能回報它 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個訊息是 , 如果你要穿過這些亂七八糟的時光 , 那麼我們在大量測量中所做的成功 , 取決於我們的能力 , 將合理的治理帶入全球空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著那開始發生的情形 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二個重點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這樣的話 , 但權力不只是垂直的轉變 , 它也在橫向轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會主張這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 已經有文明聚集在海上 , 中海的第一批人 , 最近在大西洋各地的勢力下 , 西方的獨立權 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到了一種基本的權力轉移 , 廣泛地說話 , 遠離大西洋的國家聚集在大西洋的廣場上 , 到國家聚集在太平洋的邊緣 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這就從經濟力量開始了 , 但那是永遠開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增發生在世界上其他增長的權力上 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得這不是西方的轉變而是東方的轉變 , 有些不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於它值得的 , 美國將在未來的十年 , 地球上最強大的國家 , 保持在未來的十年、十五年 , 但她握有權力的背景已經徹底地改變了 , 徹底地改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們從50年來 , 最不尋常的年份 , 在歷史上 , 我們有一個全然的壟斷世界 , 在每一個羅盤針中 , 或反對的位置 , 都要被華盛頓的一個世界最佳化 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這不是歷史上常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在出現的正常情況更正常 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極化世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直都是我們世界的主導特色 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會維持最強大的國家 , 但他們會是越來越多極化的世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	而你會開始看到在中國建立權力的替代中心 , 當然 , 雖然我自己的猜想是 , 中國的財富不是平滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國在自由化經濟後 , 會變得相當震撼 , 中國開始將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	看到印度 , 看到巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 現在的世界看起來 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 更像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一位偉大的英國外交部長 , 大眾的罐頭 , 以前形容它是 「 歐洲的權力協奏曲 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	曾經有一個平衡 , 一個五層半的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總會播放到平衡點 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林結合 , 英國與維也納和羅馬結合 , 來提供反平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在一個由獨立世界主宰的時期 , 你已經修復了聯盟nato , 也就是warsa字幕 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力對立 , 意味著固定聯盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但權力的多邊性 , 意味著轉移和改變聯盟 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們進入的世界 , 我們將漸漸看到 , 我們的聯盟並沒有固定下來 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	坎寧 , 偉大的英國外交部長曾說: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會看到即使在西方我們也會伸出援手 , 必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的瘋狂圈 , 才能和其他人結盟 , 只要我們想讓世界各地的人都能做到 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方國家獨自做這件事是不夠好的 ; 我們得要把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家的最後一次 , 當西方國家試圖自己去做的時候 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們達到400年底的起點 , 我說400年後的起點 , 因為它是西方勢力、西方制度和西方價值觀的終點 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家同心協力 , 它可以在世界各個角落提出和區分 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不再是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以第二次世界大戰後最後一次金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方結合了brettonwoods機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金組織--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在他人身上打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須達到超越我們西方朋友的共同圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為你們做一個預測 , 這可能更令人驚訝 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們現在已經達到西方權力足夠的400年底了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人當然 , 他們永遠不會讓自己參與到世界各地的調停 , 世界各地的多邊和平的調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	喔是嗎 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 在聯合國指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	最大的海軍內容如何處理索馬利海盜的議題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是商人國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想要讓海道保持開放 ,
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些我們沒有共享價值的人做生意 , 但 , 和誰在一起 , 我們共享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的看法 , 現在正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素是完全不同的 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界 , 因為網路 , 由於人們在此所說的 , 一切都與萬物相連 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們身為一個國家 , 身為個體 , 從未有過 , 以前從未有過這種情況 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關聯性 , 嗯 , 總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是關於管理國家的關聯性 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切關在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 這是查爾斯德高爾機場24小時後的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下降了 , 整個崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	在俄羅斯的步驟中有火災 , 非洲的糧食暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都很深入、深入、深入的相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家單獨行動的想法 , 而不是與他人聯繫 , 不再是與他人合作 , 不再是可行的提議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的動作既不限於自己 , 也不足以讓國家自己掌控自己的領土 , 因為國家的效應現在正開始影響他們內在的狀況 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是一位年輕的軍人 , 在英國最後一場小型帝國大戰中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國的國防對於一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強壯 , 我們的空軍力量有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是當敵人在牆外的時候 ,
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想要談談我國家的國防 , 我得要和健康部長談 , 因為流行疾病對我的安全是威脅 , 我得要和農業部部長談談 , 因為食物安全是對我的安全的威脅 , 我得要和工業部部長談談 , 因為我們希臘的基礎設施的脆弱性 , 現在正是對我們的敵人的攻擊點 , 我得要向內戰的部長談談談──因為 , 我得要和我的家鄉有著威脅 , 因為 , 他們在我身邊 , 我得要和我的城市中 , 主人談談談談談談談 , 對於我的城市 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 對於我來說 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 現今 , 我得要談談談談談談談談談
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是國家的安全 , 對其士兵和國防部而言 , 只是個重要因素 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	而是它的能力 , 可以把它的機構鎖起來 。
and this tells you something very important .	這說明了一些非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建構的 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式垂直階級制度 , 專門處理任務 , 指令結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	你在商業界知道我們時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	它是你有能力網絡的重要性 , 包括你的政府內部 , 和外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便說一下 , 不要問我關於ashdown的第一個定律和第二個法則 , 因為我還沒發明出來 ; 如果有第三個法則 , 聽起來總是比較好聽 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	shdown的第三定律是 , 在現代的時代 , 所有東西都與一切連結的地方 , 最重要的是你能做的事 , 就是你能和他人一起做些什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍方的註冊 , 不論你是企業的就是你的點子 , 你的互相連結者 , 你和他人的連結能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在產業裡 ; 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但現在 , 最後一件事情
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 女士們先生們 , 女士們也就是我們現在被關在一起 , 以以前從來沒有相同的方式 , 那麼 , 也是我們彼此之間的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 主宰我們這個國家的概念 , 已經不再足夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去的情況是 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我很安全 ; 我的結盟 , 像nato , 比他們的同盟國更強大 , 我很安全 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是如此 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的互聯性和武器的進步意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和我的敵人分享了一個命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官時 , 在1970年代 , 我和蘇聯在日內瓦的蘇聯協商 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們共享了一個命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為兩邊都意識到零和遊戲無法運作 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人共享了一個命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平的大障礙之一 , 就是兩邊都是以色列 , 我認為 , 巴勒斯坦人 , 不明白他們共享一個集體命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 一直以來 , 視覺和詩人的提議變成了我們必須認真看待公共政策的問題 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩作結尾 。
the great poem of john donne's .	johndonne的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要為誰送鈴 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 「 沒有人是一座島嶼 。 」
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	它會說: 「 每個男人的死亡都影響著我 , 為了我參與人類 , 送我不要去尋求鈴聲誰的意見 , 它會為此鋪路 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰唐恩來說 , 一個對道德的推薦 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的方程式的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的道路 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界上的 「 藍色區 」 , 他們的長輩和維京人一起生活 , 在tedxtc , 他共享9個共通飲食和生活習慣 , 讓他們在100歲前流行 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物 , 文化 , 探索 , 食物 , 健康 , 生命 , 科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	所謂的丹麥雙胞胎研究指出 , 在某些生物限制中 , 平均壽命只有百分之十 , 是由我們的基因來決定 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由我們生活方式主宰的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍色區塊的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能想出一個長壽的事實公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問美國人 , 平均壽命的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘的飲食 , 或是墨水飲食 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食品藥物管理局的金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更久的事物 , 有很多混淆 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽嗎 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	吃有機肉還是吃豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到補充品時 , 你是否應該把它們
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些激素或逆轉器呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是否會這樣演奏 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性 ? 以及我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理雜誌合作 , 和國家老化研究院合作 , 找到四個人口統計上確認地理定義的區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 帶一個專家團隊 , 來規劃這些人的做法 , 把跨文化的排除掉 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴你們那句話是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想在長壽時 , 破壞一些常見的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很難活到100歲 ,
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國 , 只有5 , 000人中只有1人活到100歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國人口成長最快的地區 , 卻很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題在於我們不是為了長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是為了所謂 「 繁榮成功 」 的程式設計的 。
i love that word .	我很喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它讓我想起了我的大學日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 繁衍成功 」 , 指的是你有孩子的年齡 , 再來是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有小孩時 , 年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那演化的效應完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 都是同一個故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 若要讓它達到100歲 , 你不只需要有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得要贏得基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有治療方法可以協助緩慢、反轉 , 甚至阻止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	僅僅幾分鐘就剝奪了你大腦的氧氣 , 那些腦細胞死亡 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩網球太硬 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 毀了你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑紋來對抗 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 數兆個有 「 t 」 的 「 t 」 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每8年就會轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們轉身到那裡 , 就會造成一些損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數型態建立起來
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像當時我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹的專輯 , 我們會在錄音帶上做一份複製 , 讓我們的朋友複製出鑄造膠帶 , 很快地 , 帶著成功的世代 , 像垃圾般的膠帶 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人的老化速度大約是125倍 , 比一個12歲小孩快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有什麼事情可以減緩老化或阻止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實是 , 最好的科學告訴我們人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約有九十年 , 對女性來說 , 多一點點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 沿著這條線的某處 , 我們在桌子上留下了大約十二年的好年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年來我們可以得到的
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大致上他們將免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症 , 和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些失蹤年 , 最好的方法就是去看世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷它們的文化 , 那裡的人的年齡高達100歲 , 比我們高出十倍 , 那裡的預期壽命是多出十幾年 , 中年死亡率的比例是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸邊發現了我們的第一個藍色區域大約有125英哩 , 在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島 , 島嶼大約有140萬人 , 但只在高地 , 一個叫做努羅省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	在這裡 , 男性的壽命最長 , 大約是美國百歲人的十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方 , 人們不但達到一百歲 , 他們也用非凡的維格爾來做 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	十二歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去上班 , 雜木 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十年的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實是回到約克里斯特的時期 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是被隔離的青銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是如此的有生力 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 偶爾會定期、低密度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為基礎的 , 用他們能帶進田裡的食物來濃縮 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出了一種未開除的全麥麵包 , 叫做卡塔音樂麵包 , 用沙魯姆麥製成的一種乳酪 , 用草製成的動物 , 所以乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米田的動物 , 還有一種酒 , 比世上任何已知葡萄酒的三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會中最常見的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲時達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看一下廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越年長 , 擁有越多平等的智慧就越高 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 與其看到運動說明游泳日曆 , 看到月曆的百歲人 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不僅對你老化的父母有益 , 讓他們與家人親近 , 預期壽命多達四至六年的研究顯示 , 對那些家庭的孩子也有益 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 和疾病的比例較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了我們的第二個藍色區塊 , 位在東京南邊 , 位在奧丁那瓦的亞基拉哥南邊 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北部 , 這是世界長壽的地面0 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是最古老的女性族群被發現的 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們擁有世界上最長的殘障壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們過了很長的時間 , 通常死在睡眠中 , 很快很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性交之後 ,
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比一般美國人長約七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	和我們在美國擁有的百歲人一樣 , 五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的結腸癌和乳癌 , 美國的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	和心血管疾病的比率是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實是 , 這種文化已經產出了這些數字 , 強烈表示他們有東西可以教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面有許多顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而他們和美國人一樣吃大約八倍的豆腐 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃的東西更顯著 , 就是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略 , 可以避免過量 , 如你所知 , 這是美國的一個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們會從較小的盤子裡吃掉 , 所以它們會在每座坐落時吃比較少的卡路里 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 不如在談話時 , 你可以無心地吃東西 , 他們會在櫃台服務 , 把食物放走 , 然後把它帶到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有一個3000歲的小孩 , 我認為這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	是由confcius發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那個飲食被稱為 「 哈奇 」 、 「 野生飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小小的說法 , 這些人在他們吃飯之前 , 提醒他們在胃裡停止吃東西 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	這種感覺大概需要半小時才能從肚子傳到腦部 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住要停下來80% , 它能協助你不去做那件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , okinawa有幾個社會建構 , 可以與長壽相關 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會殺人 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經下降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 在那裡你會自動擁有一半的朋友 , 和你一生中旅行的人在一起 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你在moai你會被期待分享彈跳如果你遇到運氣好的話 , 如果事情不好的話 , 孩子生病了 , 家長死了 , 你總是有你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起了97年 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們把成年人的生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作生活 , 我們有生產力 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著退休到簡單的椅子上 , 或下到亞利桑那州去打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在okinawan的語言中 , 連退休的詞語都沒有 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 一生中有一個字是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯一下 , 意思是 「 早上醒來的理由 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位102歲的凱特大師而言 , 他的ikigai正在帶著這件火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位百歲的漁夫而言 , 每週要捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化研究院確實給了我們一份問卷給這些百歲人的問卷 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	而其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上是非常直覺 , 那些放問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來 ,
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位102歲的老女人來說 , 她的ikigai只是她的曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半時分離 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一位曾曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣的感覺 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳進天堂一樣 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理頻道的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色地帶 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們看著明尼蘇達的禱告 , 實際上有非常高比例的百歲人 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向數據 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國長壽的人口 , 在七天的冒險家中 , 集中在加州的羅馬林達 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期六從日落到星期五的日落來慶祝他們的安息日 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	《24小時的聖所》 , 他們稱之為
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 傳達給他們非比尋常的長壽 , 相對來說 ,
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 對一般女性來說 , 平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位冒險女士來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別在於 , 男性之間更能發聲 , 她們期望能活到大約比她們的美國反對者多11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	現在 , 這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我認為它最適合說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異質族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一套非常小的生活習慣 , 以儀式來說 , 大部分的人生都是如此 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	直接從聖經中奪走他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因:第一章 , 第二章 , 上帝談到便宜和種子 , 再談到綠色植物 , 可能遺失的就是肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不論他們有多忙碌 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要被驅逐 , 他們會阻止一切 , 把焦點放在他們的上帝 , 他們的社交網絡 , 接著 , 在宗教中 , 堅守著 , 大自然會走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	而這一切的力量並不是偶爾完成的 , 權力是它每週都能完成一輩子 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有一個是難的 。 沒有一個是花錢的 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向與其他冒險家相處 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在搖擺jimbeam , 或滾動一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	反之 , 他們談的是他們的下一個天性步行、交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們會祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測量的方式互相影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化已經產出了ellsworthwreham
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellsworthwhareham已經97歲了 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是個多百萬富翁 , 但當一個承包商想要6 , 000美金來蓋隱私柵欄時 , 他說: 「 為了那類的錢 , 我會自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以 , 接下來的三天 , 他出去吃水泥 , 四處拖著兩極 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可預料的是 , 也許在第四天 , 他最後到了手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是當桌上的那個人 ; 那個人做開心手術 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	在97年 , 他每個月仍然進行二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•波林斯 , 103歲的現在 , 一個活躍的牛仔 , 早晨開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡穿上板子 , 丟棄羅斯特尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實住在這裡的雙胞胎城市 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她以升降重量開始一天 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後她在她的根部 , 1994年的凱迪拉克•塞維爾 , 把聖伯納多高速公路撕下來 , 在那裡 , 她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我已經登上了19次硬幣探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我可能是唯一一個你遇過的人 , 他騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠 , 卻沒有防曬霜的人 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你們 , 沒有任何冒險比騎馬爾•德頓騎乘的火車還多 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三個文化中 , 有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做的事是什麼 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功將它歸結為9 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此以後 , 我們已經做了兩個藍色區域探險 , 這些共同的探險家持有真實的立場 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我即將要在此提出一個離譜 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們認為運動的方式是如此 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們設立自己的人生 , 以便他們不斷地被推進身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這百歲的琉球女子在地面上下下起伏 , 每天坐在地板上30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店 , 或去教堂 , 或去朋友家 , 偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以推動做 「 院子工作 」 或 「 房屋工作 」 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合一個蛋糕 , 他們就用手做 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里就跟跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做意圖性實體活動時 , 這是他們所享有的東西 。 他們傾向於走路 , 唯一證實能阻止認知的衰退 , 他們都傾向有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式來設置自己的人生 , 這樣他們才有正確的表情 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間來下班 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 七天的冒險家祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	okinawans有這種祖先的神經
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你處在一個急劇或壓力之中時 , 會觸發一種叫做 「 發炎反應 」 的東西 , 它和所有東西都有關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢十五分鐘 , 你將那發炎狀態變成更抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們對目的、ikigai、okinawans這類的詞彙有所不同 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 而你退休的那一年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們對目的的感知 , 他們在生活中啟動 , 這價值約七年的額外壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝點東西 , 而不是賣給美國人口的難度 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向吃以植物為基礎的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不代表他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	而且他們有策略可以避免過分過量 , 小東西在對的時間將它們推離桌子 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 這一切的基礎就是它們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們先把家人放進去 , 照顧他們的孩子和老化父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 如果你每個月做四到十四年的預期壽命就會多出四次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	而這裡最大的是 , 他們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是出生就是積極地圍繞著自己 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從franmingham研究得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都過胖 , 有50%的機率會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 那會隨著時間產生可測量的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的休閒想法是身體活動 , 保齡球 , 或玩曲棍球 , 騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點點 , 但不多 , 他們吃得對 , 他們也很投入 , 信任和可信度 , 這將會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食沒有用 。 世界上的飲食史上沒有用過超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 ; 它們通常是十月份 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當談到 「 長壽 」 時 , 沒有 「 短期修理藥丸 」 或 「 其他藥丸 」 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許是你能做的最顯著的事 , 來為你的生活增加更多年 , 及多年的生命 。 謝謝大家 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水導電 ; 一扇窗 , 從輕而易舉的轉換到不透明的開關 ; 一個讓音樂的水母 。 所有這些東西都存在 。 卡塔琳娜莫塔說:該是和它一起玩耍的時候了 。 莫塔引領我們走上一趟令人驚訝又酷的新材料 , 建議我們找出它們的好處 , 去實驗 , 水槽和有趣 。
creativity , design , technology	創意 , 設計 , 科技 ,
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩弄智慧型材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用自行車和洗衣機打造了一輛車 , 讓他能運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起一輛車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一輛車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有一段時間 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們如何製造 , 這樣我們就能建立和修復它們 , 或者 , 最少能決定要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多這種做法在二十世紀後半葉失業了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造者社群和開放原始碼的模型 , 帶出這種知識 , 關於事物如何運作 , 以及它們在我們的生活中所構成的知識 , 我相信我們需要帶它們到下一個層面 , 到構成東西的成分 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的部分 , 我們仍然知道像紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼組成的 , 以及它們是如何產生的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚奇、自閉的複合材料 , 會改變形狀、油漆 , 會導電、會改變顏色、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電墨水讓我們能畫出電路 , 而不是用傳統印刷電路板或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我握住的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感測器 , 藉由打開這個小光來反應我的皮膚 。
