conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	導電墨水已經被藝術家使用 , 但近期的開發顯示 , 我們很快就能用雷射印表機和筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	而這張照片中有一片無色的光驅動粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然一般的加密方式只會在邊緣散射光線 , 但當我打開周圍的燈光時 , 整個表面就會照亮 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	對於這種材料 , 已知的應用有兩種 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而溫度顏色會在特定溫度上改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個放在一個熱盤上 , 它的溫度只比野生高一點點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以這材料的其中一個原理是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 其中的一個原理 , 所以它指出 , 當內容物夠酷 , 可以喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一般所謂的智慧型材料的幾個 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	在幾年內 , 它們會在我們日常使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行車──科幻小說對我們保證 , 但我們能有顏色的牆 , 根據溫度、按鍵板 , 會捲起來 , 窗戶就會變成開關的不透明 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以 , 我是一名社會科學家 , 所以 , 為什麼我今天在這裡談智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情是如何運作 , 以及如何製造出來的 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入地了解組成我們世界的元件 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的複合物了解不夠──我們的未來將由此構成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難以小量取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	在如何使用它們上幾乎沒有任何資訊 , 很少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 他們主要存在於這個貿易秘密和專利的領域 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	所以 , 三年前 , kirsty男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為開放式材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是我們這個網站 , 任何想加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發表資訊 , 鼓勵其他人在任何時候都能做出貢獻 , 並集結資源 , 例如研究論文和教學 , 由其他像我們一樣的製造者來做 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體產生的資料庫 , 包括智慧材料的資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要在乎智慧型材料是如何運作的 ? 以及它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解和使用的東西最終會塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿的衣服、我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道並了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	其次 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新一直都是由tinker來燃料的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘者 , 不是專家 , 一直都是發明家 , 改善從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜的 , 且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩個在伊利諾大學的科學家在伊利諾大學發表了一篇論文 , 用更簡易的方式來製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 他對化學毫無經驗 , 直到那時 , 才讀到這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中重現實驗 , 只用在物質和工具上 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤麵包烤箱 , 甚至做了他自己的vorex混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/製造師的課輔 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登接著在網路上發表了他的研究結果 , 包括所有他曾經嘗試過、沒有用的東西 , 所以其他人可以研究並繁殖它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 喬丹主要的創新形式是把一個在大學設計的完善設備實驗室的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫中重現 , 只用便宜的材料和工具讓他自己實現 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以拿起他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我想提一下她的專案計畫的目標是要強調材料的表達特質 , 同時把焦點放在建造者的創意和技能上 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子採集包非常強大 , 它們教導我們事物如何運作 , 但它們與生俱來的限制影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以 , 另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是要制定一系列的技術 , 來創造出不尋常的物品 , 讓我們免於預先設計的限制 , 透過教導我們關於材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 在漢娜的許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有一些銅膠帶 , 連接到mp3播放器和磁鐵 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho所做的研究 , 漢娜創造了一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電的布料和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其他製造者 , 漢娜發表了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都能複製並繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙本電子產品是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜又有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝作品 , 她分享她的發現 , 把門打開 , 讓一系列新的可能性 , 既有美感又有創意 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 而我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從不傳統的角度去處理問題 , 在過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人用材料做實驗 , 研究者就越願意分享他們的研究 , 製造商他們的知識 , 我們就越有可能創造出真正為我們服務的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得有點像tednelson在1970年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 你現在一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是這些大型的主機 , 只有科學家在乎 , 甚至沒有人夢想在家裡有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你現在一定要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 關於新興科技的先入為主的知識是確保我們在未來有個說法的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來指引我們 , 即使我們只能看到幾輛車前進和後面 。 但如果車子能彼此分享資料 , 彼此分享它們的位置和速度 , 並用預測模型來計算路上的每個人最安全的路線 ? 珍妮佛能想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	jenniferhealey:如果汽車可以說話 , 意外可能是可以避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡思考的其中一件事 , 但宗教標誌和好運魅力卻出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16到19歲的人死亡的主要死因 , 導致死亡 , 百分之七十五的意外與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定說出來 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時是高速公路上的年輕駕駛員 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮著 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 ,
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙停下來 , 死了 , 死了 , 死在高速公路上 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65到0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我在煞車上滑雪 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我覺得abs踢進去了 , 車子還在走 , 也不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空袋部署 , 車子全部都被開了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全不知道車子停下來了 , 我認為我們能做得比那更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想 , 我們可以透過讓車子彼此交談 , 來轉變駕駛經驗 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們思考一下現在駕駛的體驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車內 。 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡中 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你真的無法直接感受到你周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 ,
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的工作任務是將它往下導入部分的路徑 , 進入和其他金屬巨人之間 , 以超人的速度 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指引你是你的兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這就是你所擁有的 , 眼睛並不是為了這個任務而設計的 , 但之後人們會要求你做一些事 , 像是 , 你想要做一個車道變換 , 他們問你第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上拿走 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看看你要去哪裡 , 轉向哪裡 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車到不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是開車的安全方法 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須 , 我們必須做一個選擇 , 我是不是要看這裡 , 還是要看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做一個很棒的工作挑選 , 選擇我們在路上要做的事 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到錯或太遲 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信這一點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看這麼多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現在科技的存在 , 可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 汽車彼此交換資料 , 我們將能看到的不只是三輛車 , 還有三輛車 , 往後的車 , 向右、左 , 同時 , 鳥的眼睛觀點 , 我們真的能夠看見那些車子 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看到前方車輛的速度 , 看看那傢伙走得多快 , 或停下來 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙下降到零 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	藉由計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得那不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 那真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不是的 。 汽車 , 不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是立體的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	他們會在路上旅行 ,
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要做出合理預測車子在不久的將來會到哪裡 , 真的沒那麼難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使 , 當你在你的車裡 , 一些摩托車騎士來了bhoom ! 每小時85英哩 , lanespliting-我知道你有過這種經驗-那個人沒有 「 剛出門 」 的經驗 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙在路上大概在過去的半小時 ,
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英哩 , 有人見過那個人 , 只要一輛車看到那個人 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他就位置 , 速度 , 好的估計 , 他會以每小時85英里的速度持續下去 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為另一輛車會在他耳邊竊竊取一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 看看 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以對汽車的行為做出合理的預測
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是牛頓物品 。
that's very nice about them .	那對他們來說是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們該如何達到目標呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 如同分享我們在汽車之間的位置資料 , 只要分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車子裡有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我有一個很精確的概念 , 關於我在哪裡 , 以及我要多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 有點像是 , 以及它們要往哪裡走 。
and same with the other cars .	和其他車子也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確的理解他們所處的位置 , 有點像是對其他車子的位置 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛汽車共享那些資料 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以確切的告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃.威奇教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 模擬出模擬當模糊化時的情況 , 即便是在輕型交通工具 , 當汽車分享gps資料時 , 我們將這個研究從電腦模擬中移出 , 到機器人測試床上 , 有實際的感測器在這些機器人身上:音響攝影機、gps、以及二維雷射射射射射線的發現者 , 在後備系統中都是常見的 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還會附著一個分散的短距通訊廣播 , 機器人會彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此相處時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們可以避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在把越來越多的機器人加入混合當中 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你收到太多的聊天時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你必須優先處理 , 那就是預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人汽車都在追蹤預期的軌跡 , 你不會注意那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先考慮一個看似有點偏離的傢伙
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會走下去 , 你知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而你也知道你需要警告哪些駕駛才能走出路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	並且我們想做 , 我們要如何警告每一個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼能低聲說: 「 你需要走出路來 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:第一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者 , 你知道 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能在緊急狀況中沒有反應最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	因此 , 我們開始了一系列的研究 , 進行駕駛州立模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用一系列的三攝影機 , 我們可以偵測 , 如果一個駕駛人向前看 , 望遠看 , 看著手機 , 或是一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外 , 我們可以預測哪些車子 , 哪些車子是最好的位置 , 才能搬出最安全的路線 , 為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	根本上 , 這些技術現今存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一個非常令人不解的概念 , 這個想法 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 談論我們到其他的車 , 我們會在八卦的一片大海中往下走 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我其實並不知道你是怎樣的 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看看你的車牌號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們能考慮一下 , 如果你真的不想要後面的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 你要來到死胡同 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們能為所有人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車子聊聊你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路變得更安全許多 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人peterdamandis談到他如何協助stephenhawking實現了他的夢想 , 藉由一起飛進大氣層 , 並在0g中體驗無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短談、太空、科技、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	peterdiamandis在stephenhawking , 在zerogrohawking
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人 , 知道我對打開太空前線有多熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給世界的專家重力體驗無重力時 , 這真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他 , 透過基因組學獎 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 給第一批在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 「 一百個基因組 」 的個體 , 我們被定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特•椅子那事件
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力進入零度 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要在地球上體驗無重力飛行唯一的方法 , 其實是用雙重飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你拿一架飛機 , 飛過頂端 , 體重不到25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再回來 , 重量是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再、再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到八、十分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署如何訓練他們的太空人這麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們開始做這件事 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才會成為營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們也宣佈我們要飛史蒂芬霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機關 , 一間公司航空操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這麼做 , 你要殺了那個人 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們有一場媒體大會 , 我們宣佈我們的意圖是要做到一個零的拋物線 , 給他25秒的零度 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果真的順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他為什麼他想要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他說的 , 對我來說 , 是非常動人的 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正面臨著被災難淹沒的風險越來越高......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不進入太空的話 , 人類就不會有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此 , 我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們把他帶到甘迺迪太空中心 , 帶到太空總署車內 , 進入零和飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們大約有20個人捐款 , 我們募集了150 , 000美元捐款 , 給和我們一起飛行的兒童慈善團體 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedsters
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了一整個er.
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士登上飛機
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液中的po2 , 他的心跳 , 他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們所有的事情都發生在緊急狀況下 , 天曉得 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭起飛 , 降落地面 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴lichtenberg很小心把他吊成零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那 , 讓他去體驗無重力是真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在那第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 , 他微笑著 , 我們說 , 去吧 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們實際上在向艾薩克牛頓爵士致敬一個蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在牛頓大學拿著同樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個男人看起來不像個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請在這個史詩般的探險中加入我們
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家davidbolinsky在細胞內展現了三分鐘的驚人動畫 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化的化身 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖家 , 我來自一個稍微不同的地方 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看 , 自從我長大以來 , 對於藝術和真理的表達和美 , 在科學中展現出來的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很美好的事物 , 但它們都很美好 , 能讓它們成為真相和美麗的理想 , 能被科學和數學看待的理想 , 幾乎就像是科學家想約會的理想對象中的雙胞胎 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些表達真相是令人敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的理想 , 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 。 有時 , 它們是有用的 , 通常在事實後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	而你現在真的可以把一些圖片捲起來 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美是常常對不在科學中的人不存在的東西 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用一種形容美麗的方式來描述美麗的事物 , 它通常只能讓你了解這個語言 , 和研究這個主題的人的同步才會被表達出來 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看一下宇宙的常數 , 那裡有著一個人類的理想 , 在那裡 , 你看到生命必須從描述宇宙的數字中演化出來 , 這些都是很難理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我身為醫學插圖師以來 , 我嘗試做的是 , 自從我父親教導我的動畫 , 他是雕刻家 , 以及我的視覺導師 , 我想要想出一種方式 , 幫助人們理解生物科學中的真相和美 , 透過動畫 , 透過圖片 , 說故事 , 如此一來 , 人們不見得能被帶到的東西 , 並且能被教導 , 並且能被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常會沉浸在一個環境中 , 在那裡 , 他們學到的是有真相和美的主題 , 嵌入其中 , 但他們被教導的方式是比較化的 , 它會被吸引到真相和美的重點 , 並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這幾乎就像是雞湯的舊食譜 , 在那裡煮雞肉 , 直到香味不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我有個電話 , 來自哈佛的robertlue , 在分子和細胞生物學部門 , 幾年前 。 他問我我的團隊是否有興趣 , 願意真正改變哈佛的醫學和科學教育 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始了一項計畫 , 探究細胞的真相和美 , 探究分子和細胞生物學的真相 , 讓學生能理解更大的圖片 , 讓他們能把這些事實掛在身上 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有一套牢房的心智圖像 , 一個大型、破產、龐大複雜的城市 , 被微機械所佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是奈米科技專家的羨慕 , 世界各地的自主、強大、精確、精確的裝置 , 都是用胺基酸的弦來製成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械驅動細胞如何移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們會影響細胞如何複製 。 它們會影響我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們會影響我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 成為哈佛的生物電視中心 , 一個哈佛的網站 , 為它的分子和細胞生物學的學生 , 把所有文字資訊都加進來 , 除了所有的文字內容 , 把所有東西都放在一起 , 以至於這些學生將一個細胞內部的真實和美麗 , 能夠用這個觀點來研究 , 這樣他們的想像力就會被激發出 , 以至於他們能夠發現 , 以至於他們能夠發現生命的事物 , 以至於他們能夠發現生命的事物 , 如此 , 以外 , 以外 , 以外 , 如此 , 如此 , 以來 , 以外 , 讓這些學生們能夠將它們能夠將它們的生命的生命的靈感動作出發掘出來 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題一起工作 , 也就是 , 你有巨噬細胞正在流下微血管 , 它們會觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁上撿起信息 , 它們會得到信息 , 它們會得到信息 , 在外面有一個發炎 , 在那裡 , 它們無法看見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們會得到引導他們停止的資訊 , 使他們內化 , 認為他們需要製造出所有會造成他們改變形狀的各個部分 , 試圖脫離這個毛細管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達 , 我們必須和哈佛的科學家及原子準確分子的資料清晰模型合作 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們是怎麼做到的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用真相的方式來做這件事 , 這樣做 , 實在太實在了 , 以至於在牢房裡的擁擠 , 會防止維斯塔的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是一個三分鐘的讀者消化這部電影的第一個面向 。 這是個持續進行的專案計畫 , 會再走四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請大家看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些小小的機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為kines , 將這些巨大的負載物 , 以相對大小來挑戰螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	播放電影 , 拜託 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們的確是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	將資訊傳遞給彼此 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成不同的事情發生在細胞內 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	而細胞實際上會製造它所需的部分 , 來自於解讀基因的分子所帶來的資訊 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 都有可能沒有這些微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在缺乏這些機器的情況下 , 它真的能做到 , 克里斯的出席率真的很高 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙被稱作kinesin , 他拉著一個裝滿全新的製造蛋白質到細胞裡不管是哪裡都需要的 , 不管是用來做薄膜 , 不管是用來做成一個組織 , 不管是用來建造或修復一些東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西在跑來跑去 , 現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞裡 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你有多懶惰 , 你在本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 我希望各位回家時 , 想想看 , 我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們正在學習的一些關於細胞機械的東西 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們弄清楚這一切 , 相信我 , 我們知道 , 一旦我們弄清楚到底發生了什麼事 , 我們就真的能夠掌控我們對我們的健康做些什麼 , 帶著我們對未來的世代做些什麼 , 以及我們活了多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這個方法來發現更多的真相 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 非常驚人 , 這些微機械都知道它們所需要的細胞是什麼 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 。 它們讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	而他們一起努力幫助我們體內龐大的實體 , 他們將永遠看不到正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其餘的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪.布蘭頓計畫要在她的車廂裡住一整年 , 看看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱設定後 , 她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅程轉變成無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為無家可歸的體驗 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、說故事、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝基•布蘭頓:那年我是無家可歸者 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個瘋狂好奇的人 , 所以 , 在22年裡 , 身為記者 , 我學會了如何做很多新事 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學會了一件事 , 就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為了無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉我身為報紙編輯的工作 , 在我父親在同一年二月去世後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我相當難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	在我做這件事的時候 , 有很多我想要去感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一輩子都露營了 。 我決定活在車廂裡一年來做這件事 , 會像是一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓、腐爛的貓和露營裝置包起來 , 變成一輛1975年的雪佛蘭車 , 開到日落裡 , 完全沒能實現三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:那個社會在永久的結構中 , 甚至是以人的價值為基礎 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到其他人的負面看法有多快 , 如果我們讓它實現的話 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在車廂很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 我定期吃掉
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	而我還有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但 , 接著 , 憤怒和沮喪 , 談到我父親的死亡 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我得要得到全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個很溫和的春天 , 變成了很炎熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	而且在任何地方都不可能停車 , 不用很明顯地我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓來了 , 穿過了車窗 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗進入了 「 狗狗白日照顧 」 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	不論何時 , 我都會用員工淋浴在辦公大樓和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公共休息室清洗
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	車廂的夜間溫度很少在華氏80度以下降低 , 讓難度或無法入睡 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰在我的冰胸內融化了幾個小時 , 情況相當悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我負擔不起找一間公寓 , 或負擔不起一間公寓 , 讓我有了腐爛者和貓咪 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在車廂裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱能讓我太生病時 , 晚上五十英尺走到公共廁所外 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天氣設定時 , 溫度下降到低於冰凍 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	而我面對了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每晚都停在一個不一樣的地方 , 以避免被警察察察察察察察察察察察察覺 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我卻覺得無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 轉變成一個無家可歸的女人 , 住在車內 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變 。 我的智商沒有下降 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的天份 , 我的完整性 , 我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的事都剩下一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我在某種程度上改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我螺旋越來越深入憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提到我去了一間遊民健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 。 我在三天內還沒洗澡 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的任何人一樣感到沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉酒或高手 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當幾個無家可歸的男人意識到 , 包括一個前大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸者 。 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家可歸的人並沒有把我視為無家可歸 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所對藥物的反應讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得 , 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一個朋友告訴我 , 在那之後沒多久 , 她聽說提姆.羅斯特 , 一個全國知名的記者 , 一直在國際電視台上談論我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫過一篇我父親的論文 , 在他死前的那一年 , 是在提姆的新書 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在做演說節目迴路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到timrusert , 《見面新聞》的前主持人在談論我的寫作 , 同時我住在沃爾瑪停車場的車廂裡 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑 , 因為它到達了目的地 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我去了書店 , 找到了提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那兒 。 我把我的文章重新放回去 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西州
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友們一起住在車內和沙發上 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	到了隔年夏天 , 我是個工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我贏得獎項 。 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再是無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再隱形 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人工作完整且兼職工作 , 住在他們的車子裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化 , 並將生活在你的車輛或街道上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸 , 工作無家可歸 , 主要是保持隱形 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你碰到一個 , 讓他們參與 , 鼓勵他們 , 並提供他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事情 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你把錢給你遇到的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡 , 睡在哪裡 , 或在任何時間 , 生活狀況是怎樣的 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在沃爾瑪停車場的車廂 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaida , 帶領我們走過全國大膽計劃 , 提升生活水準 , 從1970年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著許多法蘭克、有趣 , 且非常有效地談論安全套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaida:保險套先生如何讓泰國變得更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人的時候 , 這個國家非常貧窮 , 有很多很多 , 許多人生活在貧窮中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們並不是從福利計畫開始 , 或減少貧窮計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭開展計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的孕產兒健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存 ,
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:來到孩子們 , 來到母親身邊 , 然後跟隨家人計劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不僅僅是孩子的死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回來談為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是在1974年的情況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每百分之七個小孩的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	女士說: 「 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但我們需要一位醫生來開藥 。 」 我們只有非常少數的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把答案當作答案 , 我們不問問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和中產階級 , 他們也是女性 , 做了很棒的工作 , 來解釋如何使用藥丸 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那真是太棒了 , 但它只涵蓋了國家的20% 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們為了其他80%的人而做的事 , 讓他們獨自一人 , 說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	於是我們去找你看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那個黃色標誌下面 , 我希望他們還沒把這個字擦掉 , 因為那裡有 「 可口可樂 」 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂大得多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們選的對象是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中是知名的 , 他們知道客戶總是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己練習家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各地供應藥品和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們去找那些被視為問題的原因的人 , 來解決問題 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論是哪裡有人 , 你都能看到船和女性一起賣 , 這裡是浮動的市場販售香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡都能找到避孕藥 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	接著 , 我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會很強壯 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 看 , 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那裡是藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 拿著一碗聖水給僧人 , 把聖水灑在藥丸和保險套上 , 給家人保險套 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	而這張照片在全國各地被送進來 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村裡的僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	女人說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	已經被祝福了 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們去找老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人參與 , 試著提供任何能讓人類更美好的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	於是我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	超過150萬人被教導要用新字母規劃家庭規劃 , b為出生 , c為保險套 , 我為ud , v為真空 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有一條蛇和梯子比賽 , 在那裡你丟骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你降落在任何有前景規劃的事物上 , 你就會往前邁進 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	像是: 「 母親每天晚上吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 媽媽 。 先行動一下 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買保險套 。 非常好 , 叔叔 。 先往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 又重新開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	再一次 , 教育 , 課堂娛樂
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校裡做這件事 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有和保險套相關的種族 , 我們有兒童的保險套 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久前 , 保險套就被稱為女孩最好的朋友了 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人來說 , 鑽石並不會讓它變成這樣 , 保險套是女孩最好的朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年引進了我們第一個小額貸款計畫 , 組織的女性說: 「 我們只想借給實踐家庭規劃的婦女 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 ,
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們身上取出一筆貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	過了35/36年 , 仍然持續下去 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是基金小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行它 , 由村民自己執行 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	而你可能幾乎看不到一個泰國男人在那裡 , 永遠都是女人、女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們認為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在協助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	而這在7月的第四日
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定提供給所有男人的血管但是 , 特別是 , 美國男子前往排隊前面 , 就在他[不清楚]的位置上 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館為我們提供了球場 , 非常適合的房間 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	既然午餐時間快到了 , 他們說: 「 好了 , 我們會給你一些午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 這一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	得到兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	然後食物要麼是漢堡還是熱狗 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	我以為熱狗會變得更象徵 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	在這裡 , 年輕人叫威利•鮑姆 , 他為美國援助工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很顯然 , 他有自己的吸管 , 因為他的熱狗被吃了一半 , 他非常開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多消息 , 也讓一些人感到憤怒 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 。 過來 , 我會去做你們很多人 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	在這一切之中 , 從七個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3比5 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你可以稱它為可口可樂的方法 , 如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的 。
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不確定可口可樂是否跟隨我們 , 或者我們跟著可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	這就是每個人加入的情況 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強勢的政府 , 沒有很多醫生
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但這是每個人的工作 , 能改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病出現了 , 打到泰國 , 我們得要停止做很多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府在否決、否決、否決 。
so our work wasn't affected .	所以我們的作品沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	於是我去了軍隊要求借300個無線電台
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的比政府還要多 , 擁有的槍也比政府還多 。
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 他們能否幫助我們對抗愛滋病 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數字之後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 好的 。 你可以用所有的無線電站、電視台 。 」
and that's when we went onto the airwaves .	那時我們就上了飛機 。
and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	然後我們在那之後很快就拿到了新的總理 。
and he said , " mechai , could you come and join ? "	他說: 「 梅奇 , 你能來參加嗎 ? 」
he asked me in because he liked my wife a lot .	他會問我 , 是因為他常常喜歡我妻子 。
so i said , " okay . "	所以我說: 「 好吧 。 」
he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成了國家愛滋委員會的主席 , 增加了預算的五倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每一個部門 , 甚至法官 , 都必須參與愛滋病教育 , 每一個人 , 我們都說大眾、機構、宗教機構、學校 , 所有人都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	在這裡 , 每一個媒體人都得接受愛滋病的訓練 。
and we gave every station half a minute extra for advertising to earn more money .	而我們給每一站一分半鐘額外的廣告來賺更多錢 。
so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此感到高興 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	然後在所有學校裡的愛滋病教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	而這些是高中生在教高中的孩子 。
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最好的老師是那些女孩 , 不是男生 , 她們是很棒的 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	而這些在教安全性愛和愛滋病的女孩 , 被稱為艾滋媽媽 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後再往下一步 ,
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級的孩子 , 四年級到村裡的每個家庭 , 整個泰國的每個家庭 , 給予愛滋病的資訊 , 以及每個家庭的保險套 , 給這些年輕的孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有父母反對 , 因為我們試圖拯救生命 , 這是救命 。
and we said , " everyone needs to be involved . "	我們說: 「 每個人都需要參與 。 」
so you have the companies also realizing that sick staff don't work , and dead customers don't buy .	所以你有公司也意識到生病人員沒有工作 , 而死掉的客人卻不買 。
so they all trained .	所以他們都接受了訓練 。
and then we have this captain condom , with his harvard mba , going to schools and night spots .	然後我們有了這個船長保險套 , 他的哈佛mba , 到學校和夜間的地點 。
and they loved him . you need a symbol of something .	他們很喜歡他 。 你需要一個東西的象徵 。
in every country , every program , you need a symbol , and this is probably the best thing he's ever done with his mba .	在每個國家 , 每一個方案 , 你都需要一個符號 , 這可能是他和mba一起做過最好的事 。
and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們把保險套送到各處的街道上 , 到處都有 。
in taxis , you get condoms .	在計程車上 , 你會得到保險套 。
and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	還有 , 在交通上 , 警察給你保險套──我們的 「 警察 」 程式 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察給予保險套的情況嗎 ?
of course i can . and they'd enjoy it immensely ; i see them standing around right now , everywhere .	我當然可以 。 而且他們很享受 , 我現在看到他們站在各處 。
imagine if they had condoms , giving out to all sorts of people .	想像一下 , 如果他們有保險套 , 給予各種人 。
and then , new change , we had hair bands , clothing and the condom for your mobile phone during the rainy season .	接著 , 新的改變 , 我們有了毛帶、衣服 , 以及在雨季期間 , 為你的行動電話保險套 。
and these were the condoms that we introduced .	而這些是我們引進的保險套 。
one says , " weapon of mass protection . "	一個說: 「 大規模保護的武器 。 」
we found you know somebody here was searching for the weapon of mass destruction , but we have found the weapon of mass protection: the condom .	我們發現這裡有人在尋找大規模破壞的武器 , 但我們發現了大規模保護的武器:保險套 。
and then it says here , with the american flag , " don't leave home without it . "	然後它說 , 這裡有美國國旗 , 「 不要在沒有它的情況下離開家園 。 」
but i have some to give out afterward .	但我有一些事要事後交出 。
but let me warn you , these are thaisized , so be very careful .	但讓我警告你們 , 這些都是泰國人 , 所以非常小心 。
and so you can see that condoms can do so many things .	所以你可以看到保險套可以做到這麼多事情 。
look at this i gave this to al gore and to bill senior also .	看看這個--我把這個給高爾和比爾高爾 。
stop global warming ; use condoms .	阻止全球暖化 ; 使用保險套 。
and then this is the picture i mentioned to you the weapon of mass protection .	接下來這張照片是我之前提到的 , 大規模保護的武器 。
and let the next olympics save some lives .	讓下一屆的奧運拯救了一些生命 。
why just run around ?	為什麼只跑來跑去 ?
and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 所以 , 我們反而會說: 「 在橡膠中 , 我們相信 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以 , 你可以看到 , 我們把一切加到我們的努力中 , 讓人們的生活變得更好 。
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在旅館和學校裡都有保險套 , 因為酒精的判斷 。
and then what happened ?	然後發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 大家都加入了
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國 , 新的愛滋病案例下降了百分之九十 , 根據世界銀行 , 七百七十萬條人命被拯救了 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則今天不會有許多泰國人走來走去 。
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	所以它剛剛展示給你看 , 你可以做點什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	90%的資金來自泰國 。
there was political commitment , some financial commitment , and everybody joined in the fight .	當時有政治上的承諾 , 有一些財務上的承諾 , 每個人都加入了戰鬥 。
so just don't leave it to the specialists and doctors and nurses .	所以 , 不要把它留給專家、醫生和護士 。
we all need to help .	我們都需要幫助 。
and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定協助人們脫離貧窮 , 現在我們得到了愛滋病 , 這次不是政府 , 而是和商業社群合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 也缺乏信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些由商業界提供的東西
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳創業家 , 小生意人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法是透過商業企業
so , that was done .	所以 , 那就完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	經費從公司到村莊的樹木移植 ,
it's not a free gift .	不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 錢進到他們的小額貸款基金 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們已經把錢帶進來了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你能借錢之前 , 你需要受過訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	而我們相信如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮中的人 , 信用權一定是人權 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像是朋友 , 但真的朋友會在一陣子給你微笑 。 在ted2013年 , kellerrinaudodemo , 智慧型手機的迷你機器人 , 可以和你一起運動 , 滑動你一杯咖啡 , 用可程式化的表情來回應你 。

and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 那是個很困難的問題 , 因為你得要建立一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 不但能負擔得起 , 還得要是人們真正想要帶回家 , 還能繞過他們的孩子 。

romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是機器人 , 用你已經知道且愛你的iphone作為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由發揮iphone處理器的力量 , 我們就能創造出一個機器人 , 讓一百五十美元的wi-fi實現和電腦可視的機器人 , 這大約是過去這類機器人所花費的百分之一 。

this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣就能讓你拖著並把這些區塊放下來 , 為你想要的機器人創造出任何行為 。

and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	然後如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以把它下載到你的機器人上 , 在現實生活中執行這個計畫 , 在現實生活中執行 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	然後如果你有你感到驕傲的東西 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wi-fi的機器人都互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以這麼專注於建立機器人 , 每個人都能訓練 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人領域中 , 最有說服力的使用案例是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	他們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你要在家裡有機器人 , 那機器人應該要成為你自己的想像力的一種表達方式 。
