but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但 , 我們確實知道的是 , 它不是十年或一百億美金或一大型人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它將取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 例如romo , 以及像你自己這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們全部的機器人 , 我們等不及要看你蓋什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和激進份子伊莎貝•阿倫德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義當然 , 在這場演說中 , 對女性主義的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂 , 全球議題 , 愛 , 父母 , 說故事 , 女人 , 世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝•阿言德訴說熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝各位 。 在這裡真的很可怕 , 最聰明的人是如此 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴你們幾個充滿熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼是真理 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 。 我想傳達的 , 比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都讓我感興趣 , 有些故事讓我痛恨 , 直到我最後寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫出巧合、先進、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直住在匿名狀態 , 直到2006年2月 , 當時我在義大利的冬天奧運帶著奧運國旗 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	那讓我成為了名人 。 現在 , 人們在macy's認得我 , 我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	允許我跟各位談談我的四分鐘名聲 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一位奧林匹克典禮的組織者 , 開幕儀式 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為其中一位旗手 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回覆說 , 這是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我離運動員很遠 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我可以到體育場 , 沒有助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這無關歡笑 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性 , 代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一個制服 , 她說 , 並尋求我的衡量 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己有了透明的反感 , 看起來像米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我發現自己在土耳其 , 在那裡 , 熱情的群眾歡呼 , 當時80個奧運隊伍中的任何一個人都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了一切在遊戲中競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應得勝利 , 但有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一股雪的速度 , 一吋的冰 , 一股風力 , 可以決定一場種族或一場比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是 , 比訓練或運氣還重要 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且有決心的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道被紅色海報報報導宣佈奧運的口號 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情存在這裡 。 不是總是如此 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們、決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中的角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要mavericks , 異議者 , 冒險家 , 外人和叛軍 , 他們問問題 , 彎曲規則 , 冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的人 , 並不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做出好的前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了另一位旗熊:三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊•薩蘭登和索菲亞•羅倫 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩個有熱情心的女性:wiangarimaathai , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 藉此 , 她改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然在許多村莊裡的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	一位柬埔寨激進分子 , 熱切地對抗兒童妓女 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 認為和一個很年輕的處女做愛 , 會把她們從愛滋病中治癒 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	而在孩童被迫收到五、十五名客戶的妓院裡 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就被用電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在我收到的綠色房間裡 ,
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種衣服 , 但它離我預期的米其林套裝還很遠 。 不是很糟 , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但 , 大部分的旗幟學家 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 普遍的象徵美麗和熱情 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感 , 很低 , 很高 , 有著深的坦克 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你怎麼能有一個很深的坦克車 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當在電視訪問中被問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回覆道: 「 姿勢 。 我的背永遠是直的 , 我不讓老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡有來自地球上最漂亮的女性之一的自由建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	沒有磨練 , 沒有咳嗽 , 沒有呼吸 , 沒有跟自己說話 , 沒有遙遠 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜的某個時點 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲疾呼的人宣布奧林匹克旗 , 音樂是順帶一提 , 音樂從這裡開始 , 和艾達遊行的同一音樂 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	索菲亞•羅倫就在我面前 , 她比我高一公尺 , 不算頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿 , 肩膀上拿著旗子 。 我在我的腳趾上拿著旗子 , 伸出手臂 , 這樣我的頭就在該死的旗子下了 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是幸運的 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現在蘇菲雅的腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想成為的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧林匹克體育館裡的那些 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我的丈夫在我說這句話時被冒犯 , 雖然我已經向他解釋過 , 我們在私人的做法通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不該親自拿 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四個壯麗的時刻所有的按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記老年人會毀掉我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想永遠帶著奧運的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是一個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	年度是1998年 , 地方是剛果的圖西難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上有80%的難民和流離失所的人是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方叫做剛果一個死囚營 , 因為那些沒有被殺的人會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是一位年輕女士 , 蘿絲•卡倫多 , 還有她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了和寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們強迫她看著她的丈夫被折磨和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓她七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了預產雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷腫瘤的繩子 , 用自己頭髮連接起來 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的指揮官來命名雙胞胎 , 用黑茶來命名 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房中闖來強暴她最老的女兒時 , 她會抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們拿著一把槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家庭存活了十六個月 , 接著 , 透過非凡的運氣 , 以及一位年輕美國男子的熱情心 , 薩夏.查諾夫 , 他成功地把她放進美國救援飛機 , 羅斯.圖蘭多和她的九個孩子最後都來到亞利桑那州鳳凰城 , 在那裡他們現在的生活和繁榮 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語中 , 地圖文是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書的主角是強而有熱情的女性 , 像羅絲•卡蘭多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不把它們造出來 , 不需要這樣做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都見到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一輩子都和女性合作過 。
i know them well .	我很清楚他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父系天主教和保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪 , 到了五歲時 , 我是個激進的女性主義者雖然尚未達到智利 , 所以沒有人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有很高的價格可以支付我的自由 , 為了質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出代價 , 因為為了我收到的每一塊炸彈 , 我就能遞出兩種 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒保拉在她二十歲時 , 她對我說 , 女權主義被約會了 , 我應該繼續走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們經歷了一場難忘的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒一樣有特權的女性 , 以及今天在座的所有人 , 但對世界上其他大部分的姊妹來說 , 仍然被強迫到預產婚姻、妓女、強迫勞工──她們有不想要或無法餵飽的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法控制自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、被毆打 , 有時會被懲罰殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方的年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是個侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情過 , 我因缺乏男性而受苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義沒有死 , 沒有任何意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為女神的樣子 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為 「 金星 」 , 或 「 金星 」 , 或 「 bimbo 」 , 或 「 任何你想要的 」 ; 名字都不重要 , 只要我們了解它的意義 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以 , 這是另一個充滿熱情的故事 , 這是個令人難過的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	地方是孟加拉的一個小女子診所 。
the year is 2005 .	年份是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫衛生主義者 , 在她的三週假期間 , 他去了診所 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行婦女等了好幾個小時被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人處於極端痛苦之中 , 因為她有好幾種腐爛的莫耳 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一的解決方案就是拉出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有為此許可 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒了很大的風險 , 且她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她已經帶了一些novocaine了 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢且充滿熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她祈求一份禱告 , 用操作來領先 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 解脫的病人親吻她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生主義者多抽出許多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人正在和她丈夫一起等待她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人的臉看起來像個水梅隆 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它是如此的腫脹 , 讓你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺死美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她做過的事感到害怕 , 但後來翻譯解釋 , 病人的狀況和操作沒有任何關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打她 , 因為她不是在家裡準備晚餐給他 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性生活在這樣的情況下 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人中最窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性有三分之二的勞工 , 卻擁有世界資產的比例不到1% 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們的薪水比男性少 , 如果她們有薪水 , 她們會保持脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 她們會不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作、控制自己的收入、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予權力 , 她的孩子和家人會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村莊
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和婦女談話 , 並解釋土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們已經砍伐、賣掉樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹木 , 用水給她們 , 掉下來了 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五、六年間 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤被豐富 , 村莊就被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最後面的社會總是那些把女性放下來的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這種明顯的事實卻被政府忽略 , 也被慈善事業所忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一美元給一個女人的計畫 , 就有20美元被賦予給男人的程式 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔了人類51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們力量 , 將會改變一切 , 勝過科技、設計和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向你們保證 , 婦女們一起合作 , 彼此連結、通知 , 和教育 , 能為這個弱勢星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者都是平民百姓 , 主要是女性和兒童 。 他們是落實的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人經營這個世界 , 看看我們所擁有的混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個保存生命的世界 , 生活品質也豐富了所有人 , 不只是為了享有特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月時 , 我看到佛南多•波特羅的畫展 , 在加州大學柏克萊圖書館 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了帶著波特羅的作品的紐約畫廊 , 已經敢於展現這幅畫 , 因為這個主題是阿布格拉尼布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的折磨和濫用權力的畫作 , 在彈性botero的風格中 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法從我的腦海或心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是 , 用 「 不幸 」 的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用的權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 強迫其餘的包裝接受現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則總是會隨時改變 , 但它們總是會受益 。 在這個例子中 , 技巧效應 , 在經濟學上也沒有效果 , 完美地運作 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待技巧從梯子頂端向下到最底層 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是窮人 , 處在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是男人中最多的統治者 , 也有一個可以虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我是透過性別、收入、種族 , 和階級 , 來餵飽我的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 在我們的文明中 , 時間是崛起的 , 能夠改變我們的文明 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但對於真正的改變 , 我們需要在世界的管理階層中的女性能源 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要在權力的位置上有關鍵數的女性 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我指的是有年輕心靈的男人 , 當然 ,
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是毫無希望的 , 我們得等他們死掉 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若有選擇 , 我寧願有威奇亞里馬塔伊的戰士心 , 主要是哺乳、珍妮 , 和玫瑰的地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它變得更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡所有這些知識、能源、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們放下我們的風氣 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造出一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市中 , 有三千萬份餐點是被服務的 。 但是 , 所有的食物是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵討論每日餵飽一座城市的奇蹟 , 顯示出古老食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡洛琳鋼爾:食物如何塑造我們的城市 , 食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個很棒的問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻是很少被問到的 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們將它視為理所當然 , 如果我們進到商店或餐廳 , 或是在大約一個小時內進入這個劇院的寄主 , 那裡將會有食物等著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到 , 對於倫敦這麼大的城市來說 , 每天都有足夠的食物必須被生產、運輸、買、買、賣、被煮熟、被吃掉、被丟棄的城市 , 類似的事情每天都要發生 , 對於地球上的每個城市而言 , 都很了不起 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿他們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘了這點 , 因為我們是動物 , 而我們是需要吃的 , 我們其實就和我們古老祖先一樣仰賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們更多搬進城市 , 更多的自然世界正在轉變為非凡的景觀 , 像是我身後的大豆田 , 在巴西的馬托格羅索 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非比尋常的景觀 , 但很少人能見到他們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	而越來越多的這些景觀 , 不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們更多搬進城市 , 更多人在吃肉 , 全球每年的穀物有三分之一會被餵養動物 , 而不是給我們人類動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由此可知 , 穀物要花上三倍的錢 , 才能餵飽人類 , 如果它先經過動物 , 那就不是很有效率的方式來餵飽我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也造成了越來越大的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 據估計我們住的城市數目是城市的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	同時也估計將有兩倍的肉類和乳類消耗 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和都市主義在手上崛起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	那將會帶來一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 60億人飢餓的肉食性動物
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	那是個很大的問題 。 若我們跟著我們 , 這個問題我們就無法解決 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有9百萬公頃的雨林被丟失 , 創造出新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然與此同時我們也失去相當於現有的耕地 , 以利潤和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望石化燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	大約需要十卡路里來生產我們在西方所消耗的每卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	即使我們有大量成本生產的食物 , 我們其實並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國生產的食物有一半是目前丟棄的 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	為了結束這一切 , 在這個長期過程的終點 , 我們甚至沒有妥善地管理來餵飽這個星球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人是肥胖的 , 此外還有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	而當你認為全球80%的糧食交易 , 現在只由五個跨國企業掌控 , 這是一張嚴峻的圖片 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也擁抱西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	而如果我們看向未來 , 它是不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	那我們是怎麼走到這一步的呢 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做呢 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要解答稍微簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 在東邊的古代 , 也就是所謂的肥沃 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是最近形狀的 。
and it was also fertile .	也是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	它就在這裡 , 大約一萬年前 , 有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 大約發生在同一個地方 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市都結合在一起 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老的祖先第一次發現穀物 , 產出足夠的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久居住 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些居住地是什麼樣子 , 我們會看到它們很完整 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農田所包圍 , 被大型的寺廟複合體支配 , 像是烏爾這個 , 實際上 , 是神性化的 , 中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為那是神殿 , 整理收藏所 , 聚集在穀物中 , 提供給眾神 , 接著提供給神所不吃的穀物 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的靈性和實體生活都被穀物和收穫所支配 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	而事實上 , 每座古老城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的 , 羅馬在第一世紀時約有一百萬公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是如何飼養自己的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古老食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬能接觸到海 , 這使得它可以從很長的路上從遠處運送食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一可以在古代這樣做的方式 , 因為在路上運送食物是非常困難的 , 這很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	因此 , 羅馬有效率的戰爭發生在像是卡車和埃及這些地方 , 只為了讓它在穀物保護區的爪子上 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張真的很長 , 可以把軍事化的購物散播出去 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:事實上羅馬是用來從倫敦出口的牡蠣 , 在一個階段 。 我認為那是非凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的胃口塑造了它的印度陸地 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀倫敦的地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 它的穀物是從泰姆斯上來的 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	這些道路從它們變成便宜的 , 主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以分辨出300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚的確也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚當然也被河流進來 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billings門是有名的 , 當時是倫敦的魚市場 , 在1980年代中期 , 在這裡操作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	真的 , 想想看 , 這真的很特別 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都用手機在遊蕩 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點像在港口上發生的臭魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市裡食物的另一個重點:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 它們很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉是個很不一樣的故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	大部分的倫敦肉品都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它就進來了 , 抵達了西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦的著名的肉品市場 , 位在上面 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	藝術家從東安格利亞進來 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女人這樣做 。 無論如何 , 鳥兒們都帶著腳進來 , 用小的畫布鞋進來 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們撞到東方便宜的一端時 , 這就是他們被賣掉的地方 , 這就是為什麼它被稱為 「 農業 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市在工業時代之前所建立的地圖 , 你可以追溯到食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你真的可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造的 , 兩者都透過閱讀街道的名字 , 這給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	週五的街道 , 在之前的生活中 , 你在星期五去買你的魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也得要想像它滿是食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一購買食物的地方 , 並且賣掉 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面 , 你可以看到 , 要住在這樣的一個城市 , 難以察覺你的食物是從哪裡來的 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃星期日午餐時 , 有機會在你的窗外流血 , 大約在三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後 , 一切改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的圖像 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 一些最早的火車乘客是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被從視線和心智中屠殺出來 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並藉由鐵路進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	而這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 首先 , 要在任何地方種植城市 , 真正大小、形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前城市受到地理的限制 ; 以前 , 必須要透過非常困難的身體手段來取得他們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理上被有效地解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從這些倫敦的地圖上可以看到 , 在火車來臨後的90年裡 , 火車出現後 , 從一個很容易被動物送進來的小圈圈 , 到一個大片 , 這樣一來 , 很難用腳上的任何人 , 不論是動物還是人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是個開端 。 火車來了之後 , 真的是這過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最終解放 , 來自於任何明顯的與自然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這就是那種缺乏氣味、缺乏混亂的城市 , 肯定不會讓人們失望 , 因為沒有人會夢想在這樣的地景中走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物而做的是 , 他們在車子裡 , 開到外裙的某處一個箱子 , 回來後面帶著一個禮拜的購物回來 , 想知道 , 地球上有什麼用處 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的就是我們與食物和城市之間的關係 , 完全改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有以前是市中心的食物 , 市區的社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社交活動 , 買賣和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前是煮飯的 ; 現在我們只添加水 , 或說一點蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是在包裝上讀到一個標籤的背面 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不珍視食物 , 也不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是去珍視它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統的一個偉大諷刺之一 , 就是他們已經把他們所承諾的事變得更加困難 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市可以在任何地方建立 , 任何地方 , 它們真的能讓我們遠離我們最重要的關係 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們也讓我們依賴的系統 , 只有它們能傳遞出去的系統 , 如我們所見 , 是無法永續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前 , 湯瑪斯更問自己是什麼 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他《烏托邦》這本書的封面 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列的半獨立城市 , 如果那聽起來很熟悉 , 一天的走路 , 每個人基本上都是農田 , 在他們的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 吃起來的餐點 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你可以爭辯說 , 食物是烏托邦的基本秩序原則 , 即使從來沒有這麼建構過它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另外一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 的遠景 , 埃貝內斯霍華 , 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同一個想法:一系列半獨立的城市 , 一小塊大都市的東西 , 上面有可耕地 , 加入鐵路相互結合 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他視力的命令原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來 , 但和默斯克韋茲的願景沒有什麼關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是烏托邦的想法的問題 , 他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的字 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	那是個笑話 , 因為它有來自希臘語的雙向衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可能意味著一個好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的 , 一個想像的東西 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 來思考人類dwelling的深層問題 , 這讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西托邦 , 來自古希臘 , 「 西托斯 」 為食物 , 和 「 托普 」 為地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦了 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以用食物來當作一個很強大的工具--一個概念工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式形塑這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這樣做 , 坐下的可能是什麼樣子呢 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我想這看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉上的表情 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	但無論如何 , 這是生活中心的食物 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間為此做點事 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是我們社會裡應該有食物的地方 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不可能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便說一下 , 這些人也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	是想到食物的人 , 認為前面的人 , 他們計劃 , 能盯著一堆原生蔬菜看 , 實際認得出來 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 。 我們是網路的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這類人 , 我們就不可能有這樣一個地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我故意選擇這個 , 因為這是一個男人買蔬菜 。
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網絡、食物在當地種植的市場 ,
it's common . it's fresh .	很常見 , 很新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為城市社會生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為若沒有這一點 , 你就不能擁有這種地方 , 當地的食物也會成長 , 同時也成為地景的一部分 , 而不只是在一些未見的地獄裡的零用品而已 。
cows with a view .	以一個觀點來看母牛 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆的humus
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	基本上就是把整件事都集合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多拜訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是溫室 , 孩子們被告知食物和自己食物的一切 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一種叫凱文的植物 , 或者說它是屬於一個叫凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但無論如何 , 這類企圖將我們與大自然重新連結的項目是極為重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 對我來說 , 西托邦真的是一種看法 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上是認知到 , 西托邦已經存在於各處的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅在於加入他們 , 把食物當作一種看法 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就會停止把城市視為大型、大都會化、不生產力的團體 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們將看到它們更像這樣 , 作為生產力、有機架構的一部分 , 它們是無可避免的一部分 , 相互連結的 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要考慮更多的永續文化 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖片能讓我知道我們需要做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	是重新概念化食物塑造我們生活的方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖像是從650年前
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是ambrogiolorenzetti的 " 良好政府的寓言 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	關於城市與鄉間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這方面的訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧國家 , 國家就會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在想問 , 如果他今天畫出這張圖片 , 安布洛吉歐•洛倫澤蒂畫作會是什麼樣子 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府會怎麼樣 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是個急迫的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們是吃什麼的 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要意識到 , 世界也是我們所吃的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們把這個想法拿來用食物來當作一個很強大的工具 , 來更好地形塑這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	數週從慈悲憲章出來 , 卡倫•阿姆斯壯在21世紀看宗教的角色:它的教條會把我們分開嗎 ? 還是它會使我們團結共通的好嗎 ? 她審視催化劑 , 能驅使世界的信仰重新找回黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , ted大獎 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal2009 , 暴力事件 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新修復黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到沮喪 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我變得敏銳意識到 , 在所有主要世界信仰中 , 同情心的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都演化出了他們自己的版本所謂的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會出現在一個正面的版本中 「 永遠把其他人當作你自己對待的樣子 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本: 「 不要對其他人做你不會想要的 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現它會讓你痛苦 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何人身上的痛苦中 , 去施加那痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來不錯 , 而是因為它是有用的 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則如同司法所說的: 「 一整天 , 每一天 」 , 不只是一個做好事的問題 , 然後回歸到貪婪和自我主義的一生 , 而是一整天 , 一整天 , 你從你的世界的中心 , 再放下另一個 , 超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它將你帶到所謂的 「 神 」 、 「 涅盤 」 、 「 拉馬 」 、 「 泰奧 」 的存在中 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的自我存在的東西 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對宗教生活是如此的核心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些奇妙的例外 , 當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖會聚在一起 , 他們會爭論要素教條 , 要不然就是說出仇恨的理由 , 或對同性戀或其他同性戀的意見 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和宗教人士談話時 , 有點像是在表情中 , 穿越他們的臉 , 因為人們往往想是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗運動的物體 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	我為什麼這麼感激ted呢 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們從我的書線研究帶領我非常溫柔 , 把我帶到21世紀 , 讓我能夠和一個比我想像中更廣的觀眾對話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我對此感到很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們沒有辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們就把所有人都對待 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們是誰 , 彷彿他們跟我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的一個偉大的任務 , 就是建立一個全球性的社會 , 就像我說的 , 在那裡 , 人們可以一起生活在和平之中 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教反而被視為問題的一部分
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然這不僅僅是宗教信仰黃金法則的人 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這個富有想像力的同理心行為 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以 , 我們有一個選擇 , 對我來說 , 似乎
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們要麼可以繼續帶出去 , 要麼強調我們信仰的教條和寬容的面向 , 要麼我們可以回到拉比 。 拉比希爾 , 耶穌的年紀較大的當代 , 他請一個猶太教來總結整個猶太教的教義 , 當他站在一條腿上時 , 說: 「 這對你來說很討厭 , 不要對你的鄰居 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉赫和其他一切都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而教會的拉比和早期的父親說 , 任何能解讀出布瑞德和迪士德的經文 , 都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要重新修復那精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	不只會發生這種事 , 還會發生 , 因為愛情的精神將我們拋諸腦後 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切成真 , 我們可以用ted的現代溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的反應感到極大的關注了 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一個團體要使用特許分割 , 最近已經在新加坡社會中擴散 , 還有一些議員想要在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有藝術展覽 , 領導藝術家將會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們看到 , 同情心也在藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社群在舉辦活動和討論 , 都在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能停止 , 不能用發射機停止 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這就是我們錯了的地方 , 完全集中在相信abstruse的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定總會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我就打算在這個直到我死去的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	而我想要繼續與我們的夥伴一起做兩件事教育和刺激同情心的思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們如此地脫離了同情心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常認為這意味著對某人感到遺憾 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但當然你不了解同情心 , 如果你只是想一想 ,
you also have to do it .	你也得做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能參與媒體 , 因為媒體是很重要的 , 協助我們解析一些我們對其他人的刻板印象 , 把我們從彼此分開來 。
the same applies to educators .	同樣的應用在教育工作者身上
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能感受到一種動態 , 一種充滿同情的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 它要求敏銳的智慧 , 而不只是一種美好的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想打電話給學者 , 來探索他們自己和其他人傳統中的同情心主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許 , 最重要的是 , 要鼓勵對不友善的說話的敏感性 , 如此一來 , 由於人們擁有這張憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏這些信念 , 他們就會覺得有能力挑戰不相同的言論 , 不可或缺的來自於他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖 , 來自產業界的船長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我絕對不會想到把憲章放在網路上 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還被困在舊的世界裡 , 一大群bofffins坐在一間房間裡 , 還在追尋另一種arcane陳述 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	而ted介紹我用全新的思維和呈現想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那就是ted的精彩之處 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識 , 如果我們加入全部 , 我們就能改變世界 。
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 問題有時似乎是不可思議的 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我只想引用最後的一句話來參考英國的作者 , 一位牛津的作者 , 我不常引用c.s.路易斯 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話 , 自從我讀書時 , 心中一直困在我心中 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四個愛》中 ,
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他把愛情區別開 , 當兩個人凝視、拼寫、彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這和友誼比較 , 當兩個人站在一旁時 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不用愛上彼此 , 而是可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	而我深信

everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道卡雷托 , 因為他在娛樂界 , 其實他在電視裡 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他其實是在電視修復中 , 這就是為什麼大家認識他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的數字 。

enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	進入庭院 , 和客服人員談話 , 他告訴他 , 在帕拉索有災難 ; 沒有人在做電視 , 有一個大型的足球比賽出現了 , 人群在休息一下 , 有點緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後逐漸地走到建築物的頂端 , 公寓旁邊 , 檢查每一台電視 , 檢查每一個連線 , 希望找出這個問題是什麼 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他走上路 , 終於 , 大樓梯 , 再來一個更小的樓梯 , 直到他抵達閣樓 。
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他把閣樓的窗戶打開 , 當然 , 有一個桌布包裹在建築物的電視天線上 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他移除它 , 問題解決了 , 所有在帕拉佐州的所有人都很開心 。

all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需用一個完美的桌子 , 等著她到達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但這似乎不夠實質 , 來傳達我想要傳達的關於羅馬的一切 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 嗯 , 我只會做比亞薩斯 , 然後我會進入內部 , 下面我會展示這些東西的成長 , 展示它們為何會塑造它們的形狀等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	接著 , 我想 , 那太複雜了 。 不 , 我會拿我最喜歡的部分和片段 , 把它們放進萬神殿裡 , 保持尺度 , 讓你們能看到聖誕節的頂端 , 以及cestius的金字塔 , 和布拉曼特一邊的棕櫚樹 , 在這個很了不起的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一張圖 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮蘭尼遇見埃斯奇的時候了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看 , 我已經開始失去控制權了 , 同時也是希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條很薄的藍色線 , 有點像是穿過這個東西 , 會把它們拉在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	接著 , 我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是收集和儲存資訊的整齊方式 , 而是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層剝下來 ; 我們把它們看成是頁面 , 用某種方式來做 。

the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部分建築物的牆壁上有黏液覆蓋著疤痕 , 數世紀以來這些結構的變化的疤痕被適應 , 而不是被撕毀 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你直接展開它 , 你看它的背後 , 我所謂的疤狀組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造較小的窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人來了或其他的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應全都被埋在黏液下 。

but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我還可以向你們展示一下 , 在那些宏偉的建築物的角落 , 其中一棟巨大的石塊 , 或者是用磚塊和黏液做成的假石塊 , 比較常是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它會變得稍微立體一點 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你走下一條狹窄的小街道 , 進入一個令人驚訝的比亞薩斯 , 通過使用雙關門摺疊頁 , 如果你像我小時候一樣 , 讀了一本pop-up的書 , 你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。

" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	" 鴿子的進展 " 讓我當作抓到的標題 ,
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是一隻霍姆鴿 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。

it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子坐在教堂上方
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天起飛 , 做正常鴿子的東西 。 回來 , 整個地方被支架和綠色淨化包覆著 , 這隻鴿子沒辦法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 牠得要找到另一個住處 , 這樣才能讓我穿過我最喜歡的東西的目錄 , 我們從最高的鴿子開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人一起生活 ; 那並不總是件好事 , 但它確實能讓鴿子再次聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我想 , 這有點有趣 , 但或許有一個人應該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他花了一輩子照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方 , 讓他們有危險的地方 , 他們會變成朋友 , 學會在午餐時間為他打招呼 , 娛樂他 , 諸如此類 。

and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於得到足夠的力量 , 一起爬上梯子到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個拉紅色的氣球 , 在那裡等著他 , 他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市外面的牆上 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在舊的羅馬習俗中 , 死者從來沒有埋在牆內 。

. that's really going to go a long way .	真的要走很長的一段路

and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正往上飛 , 往上飛 , 到達阿伯來這裡 。

and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 它就變得有必要且有可能 , 試著傳達那種感覺在城市中飛行 , 而不動的情況 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過去cestius這些金字塔對你來說很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的東西 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大部份住鴿子都沒做的事:它採用了這條景象路線 , 那是我覺得要把這本書延伸到大約四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們圍繞著羅馬競技場 , 穿過聖塔瑪麗亞的教堂 , 穿過海克力士朝河的神殿 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們差點和米開朗基羅所設計的palazzzofarnese對撞 , 由哥倫蓋羅所採用的石頭 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰柬埔寨defiori 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我向我的學生展示的其中一件事 , 因為這是一個完全的基礎化--任何規則的否定 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一的觀點法則是 , 如果它看起來是可信的 , 你已經成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著弄清楚這裡的消失點在哪裡 ; 幾個在火星上 , 另外幾個在克雷蒙亞 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但進入聖母瑪麗亞德拉的比賽前面的比賽 , 在那裏 , 球賽正在進行中 , 我們被一個足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	現在這張圖表很糟糕 , 被足球擊中了 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:有聖母瑪莉亞德拉的步調 , 有足球 , 有一點鳥翅膀 , 什麼都沒發生 , 所以我得要重新思考一下 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你真的想看到聖母瑪麗亞德拉的步調 , 這些書真的很有彈性 , 很有互動性 , 只要把它轉過來 , 用另一種方式來看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	透過巷子 , 我們可以看到衝擊在紅線中被捕捉 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥兒想辦法把自己拉在一起 , 穿過這個中世紀高塔──其中少數幾個中世紀的中世紀高塔 , 朝聖格尼斯的教堂前進 , 在圓頂上 , 向下俯瞰視著我們已經提過的比薩納伏那 , 看到和流過了幾次 ; 這裡有著伯尼尼斯雕像 , 穿越了四條河 , 穿越了美妙的布洛明尼亞米特的聖殿堂 , 停止了足夠長的時間 , 在萬神殿前26英尺的直徑上 , 來追尋我們的呼吸氣 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在內部俯衝 , 因為我們正在飛行 , 我們不需要在這個特定時刻擔心地心引力 , 所以這幅圖可以在頁面上任何方向方向對應 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會有點興奮 , 不意外地模仿建築 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	超越了我剛說的那座美麗的牆壁 , 充滿了我剛才提到的木雕 , 漂亮的雕刻設置在內部的牆壁上方是 「 ristorante 」 的標誌 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們抵達了帕拉佐州的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院進入一個小窗戶進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把信息從鳥的腿上除去 ; 這是它所說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著繪圖板 , 我們看到他正在做的是 , 事實上 , 一隻鴿子剛剛拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線會延伸到所有的視線 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個 「 理解 」 的循環 , 你只需要閱讀這些文字 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員skylartibbits致力於自行組合這個想法 , 與其建造某樣東西 , 我們可以創造出一種材料 , 用它自己組合在一起的方式 。 這是早期階段的一個很大的概念 ; tibbits向我們展示了三項thelab計畫 , 指出一個自我組合的未來可能的樣貌 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylartibbits:我們能製造出自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想向你們展示我們製造東西的方式的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快地 , 我們的建築物和機器會自行組合、複製、修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向各位展示我相信是目前製造的狀態 , 然後和一些自然系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在當前的製造狀態下 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間組裝時間 , 有五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、嶄新的、令人興奮的科技 , 在鋼筋、混凝土、玻璃中 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年的組裝時間 , 250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或是有三十億個鹼基對的dna , 我們可以在大約一小時內複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 所有這些複雜性 , 但它們的效率極高 , 遠遠超過我們所能建造的任何東西 , 遠比任何我們能建造的東西更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以為了長壽而修復自己 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有著超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將它翻譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼 , 對於我們建造東西的方式 , 會有令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為 , 其中的關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要把自我組裝用在我們的實體環境中 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 這樣我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列 , 基本上就是我們建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部件 , 可以把序列拿起來 , 用它折疊起來 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源 , 讓它能啟動 , 讓我們的部件能從程式中向上摺疊 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	而我們需要某種類型的錯誤修正措施 , 以保證我們已經成功地建立我們想要的東西 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些我和我同事在麻省理工學院的項目 , 正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩種是macrobot和decibot
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目是大規模可重組的機器人-8呎 , 12呎長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	嵌入機械電子設備、感應器
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將想要摺疊成什麼 , 排成一排的角度 , 以負120 , 負120 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 像這樣 。 所以 , 一連串的角度 , 或一連串的角度 , 你就會透過弦發出序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位的訊息都是負120 , 它會轉到那邊 , 檢查一下如果它到那裡 , 然後把它傳給鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 正在進行這個計畫 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的能帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 成千上萬美元 , 很多男人小時來製造這個8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人技術嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看被動的大自然 , 或被動地嘗試進行重新配置的程式編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它會再進一步 , 試圖進行實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了計算最基本的建材 , 數位邏輯門 , 直接進入你的零件 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nandgate ,
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 就是這門大門要做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 如同你正在建造你的磚塊一樣 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從前一塊磚塊上來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會在3d空間中給你輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始把他們想要的磚塊放進去 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它在它之前所做的事情上計算 , 以及你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 以上或下降 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1、1]輸入等於輸出0 , 輸出的輸出值會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是一個輸出1的輸出值 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以 , 真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以 , 他們有所有的信息嵌入其中 , 包含了被建構出來的東西 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自體複製 , 因為你的結構含有確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都嵌入其中來告訴你如何去修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以有能攀登的東西 , 讀取它 , 然後輸出到一個比一個 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以 , 我將要展示的最後一個專案叫做偏見鏈 , 可能是我們目前最令人興奮的例子 , 都是被動自組裝系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它需要重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全相同 , 並且有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上就是在編寫它 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你要告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖動鏈 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的構造 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體在彼此的旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你基本上可以編寫任何立體形狀或登上維度 , 二維立體到這條鏈完全被動 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來會怎樣呢 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們有新的可能性可以自我組裝、複製、修復我們的實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程能力 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	而從那你就有新的計算能力
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間運算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有的磚都能實際計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的平行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這對此有著令人興奮的潛力
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我在這裡展示的這些項目只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們為一個新的自組裝世界實施這些新技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸 , 我們甚至去過海底最深的點兩次 。 下一代留下的是什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家內森•沃爾夫提出了這個答案:幾乎所有事情都可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著不可思議的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:剩下什麼要探索的 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我造訪了威斯康辛州的貝洛特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一位偉大的二十世紀探險家羅伊•查普曼•安德魯斯 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他在美國自然歷史博物館時期 , 安德魯斯帶領了一系列探險到未知的地區 , 就像在戈壁沙漠這裡 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來 , 他說 , 印第安納瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特市時 , 我對一群中學學生做了一個公開的講座 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果在ted這裡有任何比在這裡演講更嚇人的東西 , 它會試著把一群12歲小孩的注意力放在一個45分鐘的講座上 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個問題在那之後真的困住了我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該在哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 很多人有一種感覺 , 地球上探索的偉大時代已經結束了 , 對於下一代 , 他們得要去外太空或最深的海洋 , 才能夠找到很顯著的東西來探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	我們真的沒有什麼意義可以探索地球上的遺跡 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一個未見過的世界的探險家 , 馬丁紐斯貝吉納克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以beijerinck開始發現菸草mosaic疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是從菸草植物中取出的毒汁 , 他會透過更小的過濾器過濾它 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了一個點 , 他覺得在外面一定有些東西比當時已知最小型的生命形式還小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他想出了一個名字 , 為他的神秘探員 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為拉丁文為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭開病毒時 , beijerinck真的為我們開啟了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道 , 病毒構成了地球上大多數的基因信息 , 超過所有其他形式的生命組合的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有了極大的實用應用 , 和這個世界相關的應用 , 像是天花的根除、對抗子宮頸癌的疫苗 , 我們現在知道 , 大多是由人類乳癌病毒所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	在一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上我們有了汽車 , 但是我們卻沒有意識到我們星球上大部分的基因信息所構成的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些了不起的工具 , 可以讓我們探索不見的事物 , 例如深度測序 , 它能讓我們做得更多 , 不僅僅是把表面滑雪 , 還能從特定物種中看出個別的基因組 , 還能檢視整個新陳代謝 , 那些在我們身邊的微生物群體 , 記錄這些物種的所有基因資訊 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技巧應用在從土壤到皮膚的所有東西上 , 以及在兩者之間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在在定期基礎上這麼做 , 找出爆發的原因 , 不清楚造成它們的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取了一條娜索 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常做的事 , 來尋找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們會看到的第一件事 , 是非常大量的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些遺傳信息 , 我們會看到很多人類基因信息 , 當然 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大多來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常令人驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始研究這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子中大約百分之二十的基因信息並不符合我們以前所見過的任何東西 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	我們當中的一小群人 , 實際上研究這種資料 , 我們當中有幾個人已經開始稱這些資訊為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的任何東西 , 有點像是我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的遺傳信息是大量的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對較有力的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法被輸入或與我們以前見過的任何東西搭配 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這也許是人造的 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得越來越準確時 , 我們判定這些資訊是生命的一種形式 , 至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 其實只有在它們的嬰兒體內 , 有一種非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那埋藏在這個生命中 , 在這個遺傳信息中 , 都是尚未被認定的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的人生階級 , 比如beijerinck , 會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那或許可以讓我們辨識出一種癌症的成因 , 或辨識出我們不熟悉的疫情爆發的來源 , 或可能在分子生物學中創造出新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興能宣佈 , 我和史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州理工學院的同事們 , 我們目前正在開始一項計畫 , 探究生物黑暗物質 , 以探索新形式的生命存在 。
