a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百多年前 , 人們不知不覺的病毒 , 構成我們星球上大部分遺傳信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能很驚訝 , 我們可能完全沒意識到我們鼻子底下的一種新生活階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經把地球上所有的大陸都描繪出來了 , 我們可能已經發現了外面的所有哺乳動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的仁慈為下一代的探險家提供了重要的一課 , 像是來自威斯康辛州貝洛特的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們把這一課說成這樣:不要假設我們目前認為的全面故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去追尋你選擇探索的領域中的黑暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊有未知 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇科學家daviddeutsch把理論物理放在後端 , 來討論一個更急迫的物質:我們物種的生存 。 第一個步驟是要解決全球暖化 , 他說 , 就是要承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	daviddeutsch在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出一個肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一種 , 事實上 , 已被記錄下來的歷史已知 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或我們的環境 , 或其它 , 都獨特適合維持我們的進化或創造 , 正如以前所想的 , 以及我們現在的存在 , 最重要的 , 我們的未來生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現在 , 這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	而在太空船之外 , 宇宙是不可思議的 , 而內部是我們所仰賴的 , 我們所仰賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只能得到一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件事 , 大家都知道的是 , 和大部分人類歷史上相信的相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的樞紐 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬霍金有句名言 , 我們只是一個在典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 正處在典型銀河系的外層 , 諸如此類的 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	首先 , 大家都知道這兩件事 , 有點像是在說我們處在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們處在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是 , 如果你把這兩個人視為是活過來的深層真理 , 並告訴你的人生決策 , 那他們似乎彼此之間有一點衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但那並不能阻止他們兩者都是虛假的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是的 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看四周 , 看看隨機方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 完全不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只需要朝著同一個方向前進幾百英里 , 然後回頭看 , 你不會看到任何一面牆或化學污垢 , 你所看到的都是藍色的星球 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為恆星存在於星系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都處在任何星系附近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河外 , 再回頭看 , 對 , 有一個有螺旋臂的巨大銀河系 , 在我們面前展開 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻我們已經從這裡來了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但是我們仍然處在宇宙中一個典型的地方 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 要到達一千倍的星系間空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在龐大的昂貴之下 , ted已經安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 將星系間空間的觀點從星系間空間看出 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能不能把燈關掉 , 拜託 , 看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不是很完美 , 在星系間太空星系間空間中 , 完全是黑暗的 , 深色的黑暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 要是你看著最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星就要爆炸成超新星 , 你要直接盯著它 , 當它的光線抵達你時 , 你仍然無法看見甚至是滑稽者 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就這麼大、多麼黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的光亮 , 所以很聰明的一件事 , 它會在幾光年內殺死你石頭 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間空間來看 , 它是如此遙遠的 , 你根本看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面也非常寒冷 , 在絕對零度之上不到三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它非常的空 。 真空的密度比地球上最好的科技所能創造出來的高一百萬倍 。 所以 , 地球上最好的科技的密度比這個地方高一百萬倍 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這地方是如此的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能不能讓燈光回升 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	那麼 , 我們如何知道一個遙遠的環境 , 又如此不同 , 又如此外星人 , 從我們習慣的任何事物中 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	嗯 , 地球是我們的環境 , 我們創造知識的形式 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這意味著什麼呢 ? 嗯 , 比我們剛才所說的更遠--我指的是 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到看起來像星星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 夸克 」 。 原本的意思是量子論物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	意思就是 , 看起來有點像星星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是數十億年前的樣子 , 數十億光年之外 , 星系中心的物質瓦解向一個超大質量的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了那重力瓦解的一些能量 。 一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流形式 , 以光線照亮的位置 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學幾乎不像噴射機的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在它的瞬間存活下來 。 當試圖描述其中一個噴射機會是什麼樣子時 , 語言會分解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在點擊點數範圍和數百萬年以來 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 噴射機在幾十億年後發生了 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 和模型 , 用來預測 , 並解釋 , 並且解釋 , 在現實中 , 你所發生的所有事情 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個實體系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個夸克的精確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是超面部的圖像 , 雖然它也包含了這一點 , 同時也包含了解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 信仰與其它結構的相似性會隨著時間增加 , 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這種特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那個實體物體 , 和它們可能有的不同 , 不論如何體現出相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間 , 越來越多的體現出來 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是化學污垢 , 與此不同 。 這個化學污垢具有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含著不斷增加的精確度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個樞紐 , 包含了整個物理世界的結構和因果關係 。 到目前為止 , 物理定律使得這個現象發生 , 甚至是物理世界最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在太陽系和我們的環境 , 如何在我們身上取得這種特殊關係與宇宙的其他部分 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 關於史蒂芬•霍金所說的一件事 , 我是說 , 這是真的 , 但這是錯誤的強調 。 其中的一件事是 , 它並沒有用任何特殊的物理來做 。 沒有特殊的疏失 , 沒有奇蹟 , 涉及的奇蹟 。 它的做法只是我們在這裡所擁有的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 沒有任何物質的製造方式 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 讓媒體能夠有效地影響我們記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 較不具體 , 但對開放的知識、解釋的開放性 , 也是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好可以一輪測試 , 比方說 , 牛頓的重力定律大約在三百年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 我們以前所做的證據卻落在地球的每平方公尺上 , 在那之前數十億年 , 將會持續落在數十億年之後 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 證據能發現所有科學中最基本的真理 , 就在我們星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三種對開放的知識創造的前提是他們最低可能的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 它是空的 ; 它是冷的 ; 外面是暗的 。 還是它 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹隘的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系間空間裡的立方體 , 和我們家的大小一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 那個立方體是人類的標準非常空的 , 但這仍然意味著它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製造一座自助的太空站 , 那裡有一群科學家 , 致力於創造一個開放式的知識流 , 以此類推 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 科技超越了科技 , 甚至將氫氣從星系間空間收集起來 , 形成其他元素之類的 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 重點是 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 什麼可以讓我們避免做這件事 , 除了知道怎麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 它是知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動進行能源供應 , 因為轉變將是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再說一次 , 人類的感官是黑暗的 。 但是你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 即便是現今的設計 , 向外看 , 你會看到和我們從這裡看到一樣的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	有了更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到恆星 , 行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將可以做天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最困難的科學可能是生物學領域的旅行 , 因為要花上數億年才能到達最近的生命星球 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你們 , 抱歉 , 理查德但我從來不喜歡生物學領域的旅行我認為我們每隔幾億年就可以用一個
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以 , 事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含了所有預先創造的知識 。 任何一個立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何一個角落 , 都有可能成為與我們相同的樞紐 , 假如我們在那裏所做的知識 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們不是在一個獨一無二的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間能夠創造出一個開放式的解釋流 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 這就是地球 。 所以這是一個污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而有限的因素 , 在那裡 , 和在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為它們很豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個以宇宙為基礎的知識觀點也許我認為應該讓我們覺得非常特別 。 但它也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它的意思是 , 若沒有需要的特定知識來生存宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要幾光年之外的超新星 , 我們就死定了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出了錯 , 最重要的是對大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為 , 文明在這個世紀僅有50%的存活機率 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會在會議後談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為 , 機率是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我也同意他這樣做 。 我們可以生存下去 , 我們無法生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這取決於機會 , 但我們是否能在時間內創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是所有前所未有的 。 物種隨時都滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明就結束了 。 絕大多數曾經存在過的物種和所有曾經存在過的文明 , 現在都是歷史了 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外 , 那麼 , 邏輯上 , 我們唯一的希望就是利用我們這個物種的一種特徵 , 以及我們的文明 , 取而代之的是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新解釋的能力 , 新知識成為存在的樞紐 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議中 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我所指的那種事情 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 不論是全球暖化 , 我只是個奠定者 。 一個奠定者 , 一個奠定人的做法 , 就是認真看待開採的科學理論 。 根據那個理論 , 已經太遲到可以避免一場災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果真是 , 我們當下最好的選擇就是防止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 它的限制在經濟活動 , 以及它的巨大成本 , 花費數千億美元 , 或不管它是什麼 , 那就已經是受到任何合理措施的災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被倡導的行動 , 甚至沒有被追求去解決問題 , 僅僅是靠一點點來維持它 。 所以它已經太遲了 , 可能已經太遲了 , 無法避免它了 , 從任何人意識到危險之前就已經太晚了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	早在1970年代就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將成為數十億人死亡的新冰河時代 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	現在這教訓對我來說似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能永遠知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以低於災難本身的成本來解決它 , 那就不會有太多的爭論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防措施 , 可以避免我們尚未預防的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的立場 , 不僅僅是考慮到問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	事實是 , 一盎司的預防等於一磅的治癒 , 但只有在我們知道要預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經被打到鼻子上了 , 那麼 , 醫學的科學就不會被教導你如何避免拳頭 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學界停止尋求解藥 , 只專注在預防上 , 那就不會達到 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	在當下 , 世界正在興起 , 有計劃迫使氣體排放減量 , 以各種成本 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要用計劃來降低溫度 , 用計劃在更高的溫度生活 , 不用任何成本 , 而是有效率且便宜的 。 有些這樣的計劃存在 , 例如在太空中的一群鏡子 , 來反射陽光 , 鼓勵水猿生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	在當下 , 這些東西是fringe研究
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力去面對這個問題的中心 , 或是一般性的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	有了我們還沒意識到的問題 , 沒有避免的好運 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存的能力 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	所以拿兩個石塊平板 , 然後雕刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個 , 雕刻: 「 問題是解決之道 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一個雕刻: 「 問題是必然的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何突破貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的規則系統中 ? 經濟學家保羅羅默揭露了一個大膽的想法: 「 特許城市 」 、 「 城市管理區 」 , 被國家聯盟所統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	企業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅羅默的激進想法:特許城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們提出了一個非常吸引人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	現在 , 我還沒遇到這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到了像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉例來說 , 綠色上衣的那件 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢打賭nelson有一個手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以這就是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森能取得尖端科技 , 例如手機 , 但無法取得一百歲的技術 , 以便在家中產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	現在 , 用一個詞來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	糟糕的規則可以防止這種雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能把新科技帶進來 , 讓它們能到像納爾森這樣的人身上 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司在一個規則下運作 , 說它必須以非常低的價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 一個價格低到每一單位都能賣 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵 , 可以連結許多使用者 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想改變這個規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 可以有不同的規則 , 讓企業賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有一種獎勵 , 來簽訂更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是手機公司的那種規則 , nelson從操作室中購買了他的電話 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統看過那些規則如何運作良好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變使用電力的規則 , 但卻跑進一場抗議活動 , 從企業和消費者想要保存既有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困在規則上 , 阻止他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而尼爾森則被困在街燈下 ,
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能改變規則的方法 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則我們可以發展為改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想主張 , 有一個普遍的抽象洞見 , 我們可以做出實際的看法 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予更多人選擇 , 以及更多的選擇 , 在許多國家中 , 領導者也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 要呈現這兩者之間的反對是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能會想要給予領導者的那種選擇 , 像是給總統選擇 , 要在電力上提高價格 , 帶走經濟中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到給兩者更多選擇的方法 , 那會給我們一組改變規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , 尼爾森也能取得網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的損害效果 , 規則能讓人們保持在黑暗中 , 看看地球上太空總署的照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你把這裡放大 , 可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 在外線 , 就像一個黑洞 , 和其鄰居相比 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 很重要的是 , 要意識到北韓和南韓始於一模一樣的規則 , 在兩種法律和法規的感覺中 , 同時也在更深層的層面上 , 了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分離時 , 他們做了選擇 , 導致他們有非常多樣化的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 改變我們使用的規則 , 來和彼此互動 , 以更好的方式 , 或更糟糕的方式 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個區域 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡的線上
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也是黑暗的 , 相較於它的鄰居 , 多明尼加共和國 , 居民數量也差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家都是黑暗的 , 相較於波多黎各 , 居民有一半是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只是說 , 規則不好 , 因為政府太強壯和壓迫 , 如同在北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要用好的規則來創造環境 , 我們就不能直接撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找出方法來建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國大大展現了與規則合作的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這張圖表的資料的開端 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術像是鋼、印刷、槍械 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國從來沒有採用過 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則 , 來鼓勵那些想法的傳播 , 一個有利的動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了創新的規則 , 把中國從世界的其他地方切下來 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展更新科技的意義上 , 同時也發展出更新的規則 , 中國也從那些進步中被切斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入一直停滯不前 , 就如同它在世界其他地方的領先一樣 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表看到的是更近期的數據 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它繪製了收入 , 中國的平均收入佔了美國平均收入的比例 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50和60年代 , 你可以看到它的住所大約佔3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代後期 , 事情發生了變化 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的成長開始快速趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 就能得到一個線索 , 導致中國規則的戲劇性變化 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點 , 在這裡可以看到線的邊緣 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀 , 大部分的中國 , 都在一套截然不同的規則下運作 , 比起當時主要的中國規則 , 當時的市場經濟 , 並由英國主導 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 來自大陸 , 開始工作 , 像是縫紉襯衫 , 製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 若要實現增加收入的過程 , 增加的技能 , 導致那裡的成長非常快速 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是像鄧小平這樣的領導人可以複製的模式 , 當他們決定把所有大陸搬到市場模型上時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平本能明白對他的人民提供選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫中國的每個人立即轉移到市場模式 , 他們通過創造一些特殊的區塊 , 在某種意義上 , 英國所做的是:讓有機會與市場規則合作 , 讓那些想在裡面運轉的人有機會參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港附近創造了四個特殊的經濟區:中國人可以來這裡工作的區塊 , 城市成長得很快 ; 還有外國公司可以進來製造東西的區塊 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有一個城市叫深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有一個台灣公司 , 讓你們許多人擁有的iphone , 他們用中國人的勞力 , 搬到深圳那裡 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿岸cites在同一個意義上被打開 , 最後在這些地方展示成功 , 人們可以選擇進去 , 他們會因為他們提供的優勢而被鎖定 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	展示了成功的結果 , 導致整個經濟體向市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	現在中國的例子顯示了好幾個重點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	一是:為人們保存選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:在正確的尺度上操作 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村莊裡的規則 , 你可以這樣做 , 但是一個村落太小了 , 要是你有好幾百萬人在好的規則下工作 , 你就能得到的好處 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國內的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市給了你這個機會 , 創造新的地方 , 有了人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	而且它們夠大 , 以取得我們能擁有的所有利益 , 只要有數百萬人在良好的規則下一起工作 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 提議是 , 我們對於所謂的 「 特許城市 」 概念 ,
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個憲章開始 , 專門指出所有規則 , 來吸引那些我們需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 他們會建立基礎設施──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司 , 誰會先到那裡去雇用那些先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而你需要吸引家人 , 將來住在那裡的居民 , 永久以來 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子接受教育 , 得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那張圖 , 大家會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	而且我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再、再而三地做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中被捕捉的
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人們的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這真的是建立在模型中 , 如果我們能夠在未居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從未居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新憲章中過來生活 , 但沒有人被迫住在下面 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是對領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要的領導者的選擇 , 我們需要讓國家之間的合作關係有潛力:國家共同合作的案例 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的方式 , 首先 , 成為一個市場模型的小範疇 , 接著擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 不經意地 , 透過它在香港的行動 , 減少世界貧窮比上世紀所有援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以 , 如果我們允許這類夥伴關係再次複製 , 我們就能讓這類受益者在全世界範圍內擴大 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會牽涉到負責任的權利 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的控制權 , 來接管某些行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這麼說的時候 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 。 但很重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時會出現的那種情緒 , 能以某種方式 , 能讓我們拉回來 , 可以關掉我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義的壞處在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 遺憾的壞處在於 , 它涉及了強制性和衰退的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式都是關於選擇 , 無論是對領導者 , 還是那些將生活在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而且 , 選擇是對強制和衰退的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談這如何在練習中演出 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們拿一個特別的領袖 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	肯定發生在卡斯楚 , 他有機會為古巴--迪士亞普丁為中國所做的事 , 但他在古巴島沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他的確有一點點亮 , 在南方有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在瓜地亞莫灣附近有一個區塊 , 在那裡 , 一條條約給美國行政區一塊土地的責任 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚前往加拿大總理說: 「 看 , 伊恩克斯有個糟糕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新城市在上面建設
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會撐住 。 但這將會是把現代經濟和現代世界連結起來的大門 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這模式還能在哪裡試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全把一個特殊區的概念視為一個規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓民眾在沒有強制力的情況下 , 產生強迫的反對意見 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解到 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能做出更有信心的承諾 , 讓長期投資者──即將來到港口、建造馬路、在新城市中 , 他們能做出更有信心的承諾 , 只要他們能和同國合作 , 就能做出更有信心的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許甚至在某些安排中 , 有點像escrow帳戶 , 在那裡 , 你把土地放在escrow帳戶裡 , 另一半的國家為它負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲也有許多土地 , 在那裡 , 新的城市可以被建造出來 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的土地有著巨大的延伸 , 那裡有數億人可以居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們歸納一下 , 想想看 , 不只是一、二個特定的cites , 還有數十個城市 , 將為數億人創造一些地方 , 也許數十億人會在未來世紀搬到城市 , 是否有足夠的土地給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在整個世界 , 如果我們晚上看燈 , 有一件事會誤導 , 那就是 , 視覺上 , 它看起來世界上大部分已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有土地
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	轉化成一個方塊 , 代表地球上所有可耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表現在已經被三十億人口居住的城市佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的下方 , 你可以看到 , 現存的三十億城市居民只佔地球上可耕地的3% 。
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想要為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們會是這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從可耕地的3%降到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅降低地球上的人類足跡 , 藉由建造更多人可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市被良好的規則所統治 , 它們可以是人們安全的城市 , 來自於犯罪、安全的城市 , 來自疾病和不良衛生 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到像電一樣的基本功用 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要開始建造第一座特許城市 , 要花多少時間來擴展 , 才能建造更多的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	可以幫忙手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授所能做的是寫出一些細節 , 可能會進入這個手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們跑出城市 , 去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學術界在野外出去
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 例如 , 假設這不僅僅是加拿大在處理拉爾•卡斯楚的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 也是西班牙人 , 也許古巴想要成為四向合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要怎麼寫條約才能做到 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	對此有比較少的先例 , 但那很容易就能實現 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這些 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是城市 , 在他們開始時所擁有的土地價值上 , 造成了巨大的收益 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的價值 , 來支付像警察、法庭等事情 , 但學校體制和健康照護體系 , 這也讓這塊土地更吸引人居住 , 讓這塊土地的人有更高的收入 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建造這個區塊的人的誘因 , 並設立基本規則 , 往正確的方向走 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有許多其他類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能擁有低成本且負擔得起的人在第一份工作中工作 , 組裝像iphone的東西 , 但讓那些建築物能有效率 , 並確保它們是安全的 , 所以它們不會在地震或颶風中落下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節可以被解決 , 但那些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經知道沒有道路 , 沒有障礙 , 除了想像之外 , 還能讓我們無法實現真正的全球性雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張圖片作結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能如此出色 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和其他人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	這不像稀有的物品 , 共享意味著我們每個人得到的變少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那樣的方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則管理我們如何與彼此互動 ; 規則像是 , 讓我們有一間稅制 , 支援一所研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一套系統 , 我們擁有一塊土地 , 在政府辦公室註冊 , 讓人們可以當作膠原蛋白 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能持續創新在我們規則的空間上尤其是創新在想出改變規則的規則上我們就不會陷入不良的規則上那麼我們就可以繼續前進 , 真正讓世界變得更好所以像納爾森和他的朋友不用再在街燈下研究得更長的時間謝謝
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克雷格•凡特從史詩般的圓環探險中休息一下 , 探討他團隊的數以百萬計的基因 , 到目前為止 , 發現了海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生態圈、生物科技、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科學、科技、科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	dna上和海上的克萊格•凡特 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 我被幾個人問到我對衰老辯論的評論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這將會是我唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我明白樂觀主義者極度過於悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴你們的是我們如何從閱讀遺傳密碼轉換到開始寫程式碼的第一階段
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅是10年前的這個月 , 我們發表了第一組免費生命體的基因序列 , 它是嗜血桿菌的流感 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	那花了13年的基因組計劃 , 降到四個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八小時的時間完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年 , 有大量的基因組被加起來:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳動物 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	從十多年前的思維開始 , 基因組學在今年年底 , 我們可能在三到五個基因組序列之間 , 它的數量是數百分之一 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂摩爾基金會得到一個資金 , 到今年130個基因組定序 , 作為一個來自環境有機體的副作用項目 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以閱讀遺傳密碼的比率已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有把這個星球上可用的表面刮掉 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人都沒有意識到 , 因為他們是看不見的 , 但微生物卻佔地球生物量的一半 , 而所有的動物只佔所有生物量的1/4 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是牛津的人們不太常做的事 , 但如果你曾經到海裡 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住 , 每一毫升都有大約一百萬個細菌 , 以及一千萬個病毒的順序 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	不到5000種微生物物種在兩年前就已經有特色了 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了srceri的探險 , 和大型海洋學探險一樣 , 嘗試以每200英里的速度取樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做測試計畫 , 然後搬到哈利法克斯 , 向下工作 , 美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越加拉帕戈斯 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正處在印度洋的路上 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的職責 ; 我們在航海船上做這件事 , 有一部分是為了協助讓年輕人探究科學 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只拿海水來過濾 , 用不同的濾網收集不同的大小生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時就能排序出一億個字母基因密碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這樣做 , 我們做了一些驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 被認為視覺色素在我們眼中只有一個或兩個有機體在環境中有著相同的色素
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上上層的海洋中幾乎所有種類都有這些相同的光受體 , 用陽光作為它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬種新基因 , 以及五萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經把這張圖延伸到空中 , 上面有來自sloan基金會的贊助金 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量有多少病毒和細菌每天都在呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或關閉禮堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們通過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們收集了數十億微生物的數量 , 從僅僅一天過濾在紐約市的一棟建築物上 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處在當下這一切的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	只是在數據收集面上 , 就在我們穿過加拉帕戈斯的地方 , 我們發現 , 幾乎每200英里 , 我們在海洋樣本中會看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在邏輯上是有道理的 , 以不同溫度梯度來說 ,
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	所以 , 這是一張衛星照片 , 以溫度為基礎 , 紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色是冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冷水樣本之間有極大的差異 , 以豐富的物種來說 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另外一件讓我們相當驚訝的事情是這些光受體偵測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	而這些從區域到地區的巨大影響 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許一點也不意外 , 在深海中 , 它主要是藍色的地方 , 照片受體傾向於看到藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 他們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們更有可能會朝紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	只是為了試著去評估一下我們的基因重複的狀況 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們所有的資料 , 距離探險的範圍很遠 , 這些資料代表地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總共有兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些資料放到基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們是否只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家庭 , 但是我們在環境中採集的每一個新樣本 , 都在這些新家庭的線性上增加 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	因此 , 我們正處於發現基本基因、組成和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看著所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角和動物在一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在那些大約2900萬個基因中 , 我們的基因體中只有大約2萬4千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物都聚集在一起 , 我們可能共有不到三萬隻 , 可能還有十萬個不同的基因家庭 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我看來 , 這些基因現在不僅是進化的設計成分 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為在一個基因中心的觀點 , 也許回到richarddawkins的想法 , 比以基因為中心的觀點 , 這些基因組成的組成不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力 , 已經改變了某種程度上 , dna測序在過去的十年或兩年間 , 越來越快 , 非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對合成基因組學的第一個想法是當我們在1995年將第二組基因組定序後 , 從mycocollma生殖器開始 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有非常棒的t恤 , 上面寫著: 「 我幫我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	大象有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	而我們簡單地問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800 , 另一個500 , 是否有較少一組基因組成一個最小的操作系統 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以 , 我們開始做跨性別的突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	運輸只是遺傳密碼中隨機插入的小片段dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	而如果他們插入基因的中間 , 就會干擾它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以 , 我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有各種基因 , 可以將轉移植入物 , 我們稱之為 「 無證基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能根據環境中的東西 , 定義出一個必要或沒有證據的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用一個更直接的智力方法 , 用13個相關有機體的基因組 , 我們試著比較所有這些 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現只有173個基因共通點 , 共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽視一個細胞寄生蟲 , 池塘擴大了一點 ; 當我們觀察核心組成的基因 , 大約是310年左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 取決於你這裡的觀點 , 到500年的最低點 , 到300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一能證明這些想法的方法是用人造染色體 , 和那些基因在裡面的人造染色體 , 我們必須在以鑄造為基礎的時尚中這麼做 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大片中合成精確的dna是極度困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我這方面的同事開發了一個令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們可以在兩週內合成一個50000個鹼基對對的病毒 , 只有一個百分之100的準確度 , 以它的序列和生物學的角度來看 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna , 注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始驅動病毒粒子的產物 , 轉過身來 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一個合成病毒--一個小兒麻痺病毒在一年之前就已經製造出來了--但它只有一個十分之一的活躍性 , 而且花了三年才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在建造自己的硬體的案例 , 那就是我們用生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上跳到關注生物戰場上 , 我在參議院委員會之前就有最近的證據 , 美國政府設立了一項特殊委員會 , 來審查這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 要讓現實保持在心裡 , 和人們的想像力所發生的情況是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已定序過的病毒 , 基因組都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上就嚇壞了關於伊波拉或天花的事 , 但這個有機體的dna不是傳染性的 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人製造天花基因組 , dna本身就不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正關心安全部門擁有的真正關心的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 為了創造生物戰事代理而努力 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那個研究真的被忽略了 , 在未來應該要做設計師病毒的活動很少 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為在兩年內單細胞有機體是有可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	可能是古生物細胞 , 那些我們在十年內就有的細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	因此 , 我們現在正在製造數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以將種子和進入這種人造染色體的基因改造 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 要怎麼把其他所有人都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源的重組系統 , 將這些組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , 迪諾occusradiodurans , 它可以承受三百萬個雷射 , 且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	它在這個放射線爆裂後 , 會在大約12到24小時內重新組合起來 , 在它的染色體真的會被炸掉 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能存在於外太空 , 由於我們在那兒的旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一台玻璃貝克 , 經過約50萬拉德輻射之後 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 微生物坐在底部 , 變得更快樂 , 更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡是一張實際發生的圖片:這張圖的上方顯示了一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體真的被打破了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	相同的dna在24小時後會自動重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的令人驚訝的是 , 這些有機體能做到 , 我們可能有數千種 , 如果不是數萬種 , 在這個星球上 , 不同的物種能夠做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組合之後 , 第一步只是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此 , 我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 也為了希望能有環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們排序的第三個有機體 , 甲烷佔據了jannaschii , 它活在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 它所有的碳都來自於它從環境中捕捉到的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以 , 我們知道很多不同的路徑 , 現在有數千種不同的生物 , 存在於二氧化碳之外 , 可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從石油取得合成過程中使用碳 , 我們有機會從大氣中捕捉碳 , 將之轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物存在於一氧化碳中 , 我們用作為減少水分的力量 , 來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多途徑可以被工程化代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威有一項重大計畫 , 目的是要捕捉並將氣體田的甲烷轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	在短暫的時間內 , 我認為將會有一個新領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為 , 有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣闊的基因陣列重組 , 以及同性戀的重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可能可以製造出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物 , 透過篩選 , 不論你是針對氫產量的篩選 , 或化學產量 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因的作用將會在接觸到的範圍內
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用 , 直接從陽光中產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節 , 我們有一種氧氣敏感的氫化劑 , 我們認為將完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合纖維酶 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單的糖和發酵在同一個細胞中 , 以產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	藥品生產已經在使用微生物的大型實驗室裡了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學性質 , 比我們最好的化合物更複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為 , 未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能量的來源 , 環保的補救 , 或許還能取代石化產業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我用倫理和政策研究來做個結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年將實驗的開始延遲 , 直到我們完成了一年半的生物倫理審查 , 來評估我們是否該嘗試去製造一個人工物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是一項很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都把他們的經文當作法律書籍 , 他們找不到任何東西禁止製造生命 , 所以它一定是沒問題的 。 唯一的終極顧慮是生物戰場的面向 , 但給了我們 , 要開始做這些實驗 , 才會有我們所做的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前sloan基金會剛剛資助一個多制度的研究 , 找出對社會有何風險和利益 , 以及科學團隊的規則 , 例如我自己應該在這個領域中使用 , 我們正嘗試設立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的議題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們能否設計一些東西來產生乾淨能源 , 也許能革新開發中國家能做些什麼 , 並透過各種簡單的過程提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家philipzimbardo說過 「 快樂 」 和 「 成功 」 都是根深蒂固的 , 大部分人都不理想:我們朝向過去、現在和未來邁進的方式 。 他建議我們準時校正我們的觀點 , 成為改善我們人生的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、幸福、思想、心理、科學、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開出一個健康的準確度 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的點子 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始時鐘拜託 。 30秒鐘的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	讓它保持安靜 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	大約是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們來談談亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來亞當 , 別這麼想 , 吃點東西 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一咬一口 , 亞當 。 別棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 ,
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好的 。 一口 , 地獄是什麼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑的 。 一切都是為了產出、抗拒 , 是的 , 不 , 現在 , 後來 , 衝動 , 反思 , 目前的焦點和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落入當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	青少年的女孩們 , 在婚姻中 , 她們承受了性吸引和處女 , 感謝布希總統 , 百分之六十 , 在一年之內 , 因性誘惑而產生 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部分都不用生育控制就這麼做了 。
so much for promises .	這麼多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓四歲的孩子誘惑 , 給他們一個治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然是付錢的 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 等待 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	會發生的是三分之二的孩子 , 給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 現在他們延後了 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特•米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛的同事 , 十四年後回去嘗試發掘那些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	學生之間有很大的差異 , 他們抗拒和孩子 , 在很多方面都是如此 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒分數的孩子們 , 坐下的分數高達250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 。 那就像是一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有遇到那麼多麻煩 。 他們是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且有決心的 。 至今 , 對我來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是未來的焦點 , 而不是當下的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀是研究個人、我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動分成時間區或時間分類 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而你會自動、無意識地做這件事 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	他們在文化、國家之間、個人、社會階級、教育水平之間的差異 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 他們可以變得有偏見 , 因為你學會過度使用其中的一些東西 , 讓其他人使用 。
what determines any decision you make ?	什麼決定了你做的任何決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	做一個決策 , 決定你要做一個行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在立即的情況下 , 別人在做什麼 , 以及你感受到什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們以這種形式做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現狀 」 , 因為他們的焦點就是現在的樣子 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不相關的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是在說 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況是什麼樣的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以 , 他們的決定是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們打算把那些人稱為 「 過去 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在 「 是什麼 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是當下 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們將稱之為 「 未來 」 。 他們的焦點在於將來會是什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要辯論 , 時間觀點的悖論 , 是影響你所做的每一決定 , 你完全沒意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	意思是 , 這種程度上你有偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	其實有六種 。 有兩種呈現方式 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式是過去的 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在 「 過度積極 」 或 「 過度負面 」 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是現代主義的 , 取名為 , 你把焦點放在生活的喜悅上 , 或是當前的時尚主義者--這並不重要 , 你的人生被控制了 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來的、設定目標的 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者是超然的未來:命名為 , 生命始於死後 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出心理靈活性 , 轉換時間觀點的流暢度 , 取決於局面的需求 , 這就是你得學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時空檔 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高於過度積極 , 未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	以及現代主義的調適 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	永遠低於過去的負面和現況主義 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳的顳葉混合體是你從過去的積積極帶給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份 , 以及你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來得到的 , 是翅膀到翱翔 , 到新的目的、新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	從現在的享樂主義得到的 , 是能量 , 探索自己、位置、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	以外的任何時間觀點都有比正面更多的負面觀點 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲了什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 。 他們犧牲朋友時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲好玩的時間 。 他們犧牲了個人的侮辱 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲嗜好 , 犧牲睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	而他們為工作、成就和控制而生活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我有共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯貧民區長大 , 一個住在過去和現在的西爾家庭 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我身為一個未來優秀的人 , 走過頂端的人 , 做這些犧牲的人 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我有未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到其中兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了現代主義 , 我把焦點加到過度積極的程度 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們正把這個應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學率、結合成癮率、增強青少年健康、用時間比喻來治好ptsd , 讓奇蹟能夠促進永續性和保育 , 降低身體復健率 , 讓50%的輟學率下降 , 轉變為自殺恐怖分子 , 並將家庭衝突改為時間軸 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以 , 我想以此來結尾:許多生命的謎題 , 可以透過了解你的時間觀 , 和其他人的觀點來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深奧 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	今天的頭條有多少人在100年內會很重要 ? 1000年 ? kirkcitron的 「 長期新聞 」 計畫收集了現今不只重要的故事 , 數十年甚至數世紀以來 , 還會產生共鳴 。 在ted1010年 , 他發起了近期的頭條 , 用潛力來形塑我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學等 ,
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞
we are drowning in news .	我們在新聞中淹沒 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單單靠突發者每年就有350萬則新聞報導 。
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來說 , 那些故事中有多少會很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長遠新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個由長久以來的現在基金會成立的項目 , 由tedsters成立 , 包括kevinkellly和stewart品牌 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們在尋找的 , 是關於50、100或10 , 000年後的新聞 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	而當你透過那個過濾器看新聞時 , 很多的情況下跌了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 從a.p.p.這裡拍攝的頂尖故事 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年內會有什麼影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但 , 過去一年的頂尖故事是經濟 , 我只是賭 , 遲早或後來 , 這種特定的衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	那麼 , 什麼樣的故事可能會對未來造成影響呢 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 我們拿科學來說吧 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會透過我們的血液修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	有一天你已經來到這裡了 , 如果你是老鼠 ,
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些近期的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液將基因送進大腦裡 , 一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	那資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今天我們已經有60億的麻煩餵飽 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國不會因為基因改造作物而餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經賭上十億的研究 。
what about global politics ?	那全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界在何時會非常不同 , 如果中國設定議程 , 他們就有可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經克服了美國作為世界最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們開始在孩子們身上做dna檢測 , 來選擇他們的職業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各種方法來推回我們所知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些近期的發現:在阿根廷有一個螞蟻蟻群 , 現在已經散播到每一塊大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自主的機器人科學家 , 很快就發現了一項發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命也不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來 , 或沒有我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但 , 過去一年 , 我挑選的長篇新聞是這個:月球上的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓蟻群在上面放置容易多了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這麼做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫一支大支票 。
