my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長期來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他人更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡洛琳.帕羅科展現了從卡西尼航程到土星的影像 , 專注於它最大的月球、土衛六 , 以及在凍土衛二上 , 似乎射擊冰層的噴射流 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、太空、科技、宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛過我們來土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一段你和我多年來的旅程 , 開始於50年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不只在月球上實體上設定了腳步 , 還把機械飛行器送到所有行星上 , 我們已經登陸過小行星 , 我們已經用彗星登陸 , 此時此刻 , 我們在太空船上有一艘太空船 , 以冥王星為名的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	而所有這些機器人的任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一個了解事物的旅程 , 去了解我們宇宙的地方 , 去了解我們的起源 , 以及地球 , 我們的地球 , 和我們 , 生活在上面 , 漸漸成真 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在所有太陽系中 , 我們可能去的地方 , 尋找類似這樣的問題的答案 。 土星在1980年代早期我們造訪過土星之前 。 但是我們對土星的調查 , 自從卡西尼號太空船以來 , 在星際空間旅行七年以來 , 飛行到土星的軌道上 , 在2004年的夏天 , 最具體的機器人暴露在太陽周圍 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘的、科學的洞見 , 並且顯然超越了比較 , 而這個系統的調查卻有著巨大的宇宙接觸 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就立即學會了很多關於星星的光碟和氣體 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的圖片是andromedanebula , 它是我們最接近的 , 最大的螺旋星系到銀河系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	然後 , 這裡是一幅漂亮的複合體 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程真的是其中的一部分 , 也是人類旅程的比喻 , 來了解我們周遭所有事物的相互連結 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片的比喻 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們 , 我們在卡西尼學會時所學到的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們在過去兩年半所拍攝的所有漂亮照片 , 因為我只是沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要集中在兩個最令人興奮的故事中 , 在這個重大探索探險的探險中 , 我們正在進行土星 , 過去兩年半以來一直都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星被一個非常大且多樣化的月球收集在一起 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里寬到全美各地 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝的漂亮圖片 , 事實上 , 用它的月亮來呈現土星 。 這裡是土星和衛星 , 這裡是土星 , 這裡是土星 , 顯示環狀的邊緣 , 顯示它們有多垂直的薄度 , 和土衛二的相似 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47個月球中有兩個是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	而這些是土衛六和土衛六 。 土衛六是土星最大的月球 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡 , 是目前為止最大的未被探索的地形 , 是我們在太陽系中剩下的 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這種身體有著很長的好奇心 , 看過行星的人 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境比較像是我們在地球上這裡的環境 , 或至少在過去曾經擁有的環境 , 比起太陽系中的任何其他身體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣主要是分子氮氣 , 就像你在座的各位呼吸一樣 , 除了它的大氣被簡單的有機物質混淆 , 像是甲烷和丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子在土衛六的大氣層高處會被破解 , 它們的產品會加入一起 , 製造出霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀物無所不在 。 它完全是全球性和信封的土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也是為什麼你看不到我們眼睛在光譜上可見的區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些嗜鹽粒子 , 它被保持在卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 經過數十億年 , 溫柔地漂移到水面上 , 覆蓋在厚有機ludge的表面 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以就像泰坦一樣 , 相當於焦油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 在泰坦的表面溫度下可以是液態的 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是為了土衛六 , 海水對地球的含量 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可以調整的 , 所以要體認到這個情況帶給整個前景一個奇異的可能性的世界 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 好 , 在雲層之上方 , 你有數百公里的霧狀物 , 防止任何陽光到達表面 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	表面的溫度是華氏零下的350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管如此寒冷 , 你還是可以下雨落在土衛六表面 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 大雨在地球上所做的事:它雕刻了海鷗 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能創造峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石坑中池塘 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把高山峰和山丘洗掉 , 放到低地上 。 所以停下來思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六表面的樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六上的高中正如地球上的深海漫遊一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	它很寒冷 , 很悲慘 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密歇根湖的邊緣 , 帶著油漆的薄膜 , 站在密歇根州 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	那是我們在卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 土衛六表面的觀點 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現了什麼 , 雖然在細節上不一樣 , 每個故事都和那個故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼族人──那就像是朱利斯凡爾納冒險──成真了 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有厚厚、延伸的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 被太陽照射後 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	然而 , 另一個月亮 , 我甚至不知道是哪一個 。 這是非常廣闊的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器可以透過這個大氣層看到向下的表面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	而你看到的是明亮又深色的區域 , 這差不多對我們來說都是如此 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	真是太神秘了:我們不能把我們在土衛六上看到的東西做出來 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近看這個區域時 , 你開始看到一些東西 , 像是我們不認識的辛格管道 。 你看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上 , 一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面上很少有隕石坑 , 意即 , 它是非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	而有些特徵看起來是板塊的 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了一樣 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到一個星球上有任何線性時 , 它就意味著有一個斷層 , 像個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它的構造已經改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但是我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道的六個月後 , 一個事件發生了 , 許多人都認為是卡西尼號調查的高點 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是惠更斯探測器的部署 , 歐布西尼探測器探測卡西尼號在整個太陽系中承載了七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時的時間 , 讓它降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這個事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在人類史上第一次登陸外太陽系 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	意義重大的是 , 在我心目中 , 這個事件應該要在美國和歐洲各個城市都在慶祝貼紙遊行 , 可悲的是 , 這不是這樣 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這對另一個原因是顯著的 。 這是個國際的使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國、慶祝時報 , 都在英文口音中被賦予 , 還有美國口音 , 德文口音 , 和法國人 , 和義大利人和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	那是一舉一動的示範 , 說明 「 聯合國 」 應該是什麼意思:一個真正的聯合國 , 加入了一項對好的競技努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 探究一個星球是大規模的 , 並且了解一個地球系統 , 對於人類歷史來說 , 人類是無法觸及的 , 現在人類已經觸及它了 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我剛剛提到雞皮疙瘩了 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極大的情感事件 , 我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不該忘記 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但無論如何 , 探測器在下降的路上進行測量 , 同時也拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看到土衛六表面的第一張照片 , 從探測器出來的樣子 。 這是我們所看到的 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那真是令人震驚 , 因為那是我們希望其他照片從軌道上拍到的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個不可思議的圖案 , 地質圖案 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這是一種趨勢的排水模式 , 只能由液體的流動形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以跟著這些管道 , 看看它們是如何轉換的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	然後他們轉換成這條通道 , 這條通道流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是流體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這卻是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在八公里內拍的 , 好嗎 ? 同樣地 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是一架航空高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機穿越美國 , 你會在這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是你在鐵達尼航空的窗口飛過土衛六表面的圖片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器來到海面上 , 我要給你們看 , 女士們 , 先生們 , 這是第一張從外太陽系的月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是水的冰塊 , 是嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它降落在其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 且它沒有從視線下沉 。 所以它不是我們登陸的流體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	探測器的下降基本上相當於泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一塊沒有鞏固的地面 , 被液態甲烷所困住 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	可能是這種材料已經在土衛六的高地上被沖洗掉 , 透過我們看到的這些管道 , 經過了數十億年的時間 , 來填滿低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器登陸的目的 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 在我們的影像中沒有任何跡象 , 甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體都沒有 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 我們發現沙丘時 , 會變得更加困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好的 , 這是我們在赤道地區的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高達100公尺 , 被幾公里的距離分開 , 它們會持續數英里、里程數 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	那裡有數百英里 , 高達一千或一百二百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再說一次 , 它變得很困惑 , 沒有體液 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地地區的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在泰坦的南極地區有一個湖泊的景象 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大約和安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 僅僅一個星期半前 , 我們飛過土衛六的北極 , 再次發現 , 這裡有卡斯皮亞海的一個特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 基於某些我們不了解的理由 , 或至少在這個季節 , 很明顯地在土衛六的極點 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是個很了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它是外星人 , 但卻很奇特的地球形態 , 和極大的地質形成 , 和極大地理多樣性 , 是個迷人的世界 , 它只能在太陽系中享有複雜性和豐富性是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小衛星 , 大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到在英格蘭旁邊 , 只是為了展示它的大小 。 這不是一個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二是很白的 , 它的表面很亮 , 它的表面很明顯和骨折一樣 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但土衛二之母在南極發現了土衛二的發現 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 在那裡 , 我們發現了這種骨折的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	而它們是不同的顏色 , 因為它們是不同的組成 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋 。 這些骨折被有機物質包裹起來 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個區域 , 整個南極地區 , 都有高溫 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	那就如同發現地球上的南極洲一樣熱 , 比熱帶地區還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍了額外的照片 , 我們發現從這些骨折中 , 會發出微弱的噴射流 , 冰粒會延伸到數百英里的太空中 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張圖片編碼出來時 , 我們看到這些噴射機餵飽一個質量 , 事實上 , 我們看到 , 在其它影像中 , 上千英里進入土衛二上空的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊都檢查過像這樣的圖像 , 就像這張 , 思考了卡西尼號的其他成果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射機可能是從土衛二表面下的液態水噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有 , 可能是液態水、有機物質 , 以及過剩的熱量 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 或者 , 換句話說 , 一個可能適合生命體的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴你們 , 我們太陽系其他地方的生命發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其他地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能夠證明 , 基因的發生率不止一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立在我們的太陽系中 , 那就意味著 , 推斷 , 它在整個宇宙中發生了驚人的次數 , 以及它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍然是我們所知唯一的行星 , 就是生命 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它是珍貴的 , 它是獨一無二的 , 目前為止 , 我們唯一認識的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代被警示和連貫 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果不是的話 , 你們會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次 , 地球是從太空中拍攝出來的 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置有著巨大的影響 , 以及我們對地球的保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	嗯 , 我們在卡西尼號上拍攝了相當先前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它完全是太陽的日全食 , 從土星的另一端看 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張不可能美麗的圖片中 , 你看到主要的光環被太陽照射 , 你看到太陽折射的影像 , 你看到這個光環是由土衛二的表面所創造的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但就好像那還不夠聰明 , 我們可以發現 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 在土星光環的臂彎中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 有一些深刻的動作 , 就是從外星人身上看到自己 , 並且捕捉到我們小小的藍色行星在其他世界的天空中 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	那 , 以及我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個半個世紀前開始的發現之旅中得到的最好的獎賞 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	2005年 , 全世界只有15%的人被繪製出來 。 這讓援助在災難過後的速度慢下來 , 並隱藏了未被使用的土地和未知的道路 。 在這個短短的演講中 , 谷歌的拉特•卡拉加達•德摩斯繪製出一個團體繪製工具 , 全球各地的人都在使用繪製他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作 , 設計 , 地圖 , 科技 , 科技 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	laliteshkatragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體系 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , cyclonenargiss毀了manmar 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人受到嚴重的幫助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想把人趕到面積上
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路地圖 , 也沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有幫助到達周圍受害者的地圖 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看一張洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信 , 在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人口被描繪成可辨識的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國總統開頭的問題是世界上絕大多數的民眾臉孔:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但 , 協助來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40位志願者用一個新的軟體來繪製120 , 000公里的道路 , 30000間醫院、物流和解放點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一種能賦予我們每一個人的能力 , 來繪製我們所知的地圖 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有的東西 , 從道路到河流 , 從學校到當地企業 , 視頻商店到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎得主赫南多•德索托承認 , 大部分發展中國家的經濟利益的關鍵在於將大量未謀殺的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 單單在印度 , 一兆美元的房地產尚未完成 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是在去年 , 170個國家就有數千名使用者已經繪製出數百萬個資訊 , 並創造出一個程度的細節地圖 , 從來沒有想過可行 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	而這是由各地熱情使用者的力量所產生的 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看一些使用者所創造的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 如我們所說 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們正在繪製這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到塞內加爾剛繪製一條道路的橋樑 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	而且 , 離家更近 , 查盧亞 , 在班加羅爾的一個ng.g.道路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算機幾何學的結果 , 手勢辨識 , 以及機器學習 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計的使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個用戶 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是我們未開發的地球70%的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村落布德鲁斯山一趟十個月的非暴力抗爭 , 阻止一個障礙 , 穿過他們的橄欖球場 。 你聽過嗎 ? 不這麼想 。 巴西的電影製作人朱利亞•巴哈問為什麼我們只注意在以色列巴勒斯坦衝突中的暴力 , 而不是在有一天可能帶來和平的非暴力領袖 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、慈悲、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的作品 , 他們試圖用和平手段來終結衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我和歐洲及美國的作品一起旅行時 , 有一個問題總是會出現:巴勒斯坦甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回來 , 在那裡 , 我花了我的時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和定居者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者試圖鑄造大規模的國家非暴力運動 , 來結束佔領 , 並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	然而 , 在座的大多數人可能從來沒有聽過他們的話 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分裂在地面上和感知上發生的事情之間的分歧 , 是我們目前還沒有巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的關鍵原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天在這裡要談的是注意力的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及西岸的非暴力運動的出現和發展 , 加薩和其他地方 , 但今天 , 我的個案研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 要培養出非暴力行為主要缺少的 , 並不是為了巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力行為 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經是的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用布德鲁斯的這個村莊來說明一下這一點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建立一個分離障礙 , 而這個障礙的一部分會被蓋在村莊的頂端 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並被包圍 , 所以他們會失去自由地取得西岸的餘地 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過受當地領導的啟發 , 他們發起了一個和平抗藥性的活動 , 來阻止這發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你看一些短片 , 所以你對在地面上實際的樣子有種感覺 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知牆壁會將巴勒斯坦和以色列分開 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯這裡 , 我們了解到牆壁會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:柵欄有 , 事實上 , 造成了恐怖的解決方案 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男:今天你被邀請去一場和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十個以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列積極份子:軍隊比非暴力反對者更嚇壞軍隊 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女士:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但沒有一個人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	fatah黨員:我們必須排除傳統思維的思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯派對成員:我們處在完全和諧的狀態 , 我們想要把它散播到所有的巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	聊天:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	fatah , 哈馬斯和熱門的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	新聞主持人:在柵欄上方的衝擊持續下去 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被送去分散群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像是落珠 。 到處射擊 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列積極份子:我確信我們都要死了 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊有其他人甚至不是牛仔 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗議不會阻止[不清楚]
protester: this is a peaceful march .	妓女:這是一場和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	聊天:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	茱莉亞巴查:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體無法報導七年前發生的非凡事件 , 2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯成功的事實 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民們 , 經過了10個月的和平抗爭之後 , 說服了以色列政府 , 把障礙的路線從他們的土地上移到綠線 , 也就是國際上認可了以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯的抗爭自此傳播到西岸到巴勒斯坦的鄰里到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體卻保持在這些故事上大部分的沉默 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種寂靜帶有深遠的後果 , 導致非暴力的可能性成長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦存活下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗拒和非暴力抗爭 , 共有一件非常重要的事 ; 他們都是戲院的形式 , 尋求觀眾的成因 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷得到前額葉的封面 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題 , 對於非暴力領導人來說 , 對於他們的社區來說 , 公民不服從是可行的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	注意力的力量可能不會對房間裡的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	要讓你的孩子丟出越來越大聲的trums , 最好的辦法就是給他注意 , 他第一次丟一個符號 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	腫瘤會變成兒童心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 既然孩子已經學到他可以從中得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予或戒斷孩子的注意力來獎勵或獎勵行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以受到影響 , 取決於國際社群選擇集中注意力的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 在結束中東衝突的核心 , 並將和平帶給我們 , 來把非暴力行為轉化成功能性行為 , 做法是讓更多關注現今在地面上的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在將我的影片帶到西岸的村落 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷 , 我見識過即使是一部紀錄片也可能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫瓦拉杰的村莊 , 位在離耶路撒冷很近的村落裡 , 社區面臨著和布德鲁斯非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有取得自由 , 不論是西岸還是耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	兩年來 , 他們一直在使用非暴力行為 , 但從沒有人在注意 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們整理了一個篩檢 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉辦了最好、最精緻的示威 , 來約會 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民們 , 看到布德鲁斯在一部電影中記錄下來的故事 , 覺得確實有人在追隨他們在做什麼 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續走下去 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這一邊 , 有一種新的和平運動 , 叫做 「 孤立驅動 」 , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導人一直用布德鲁斯作為他們主要的招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說以色列人從來沒有活躍過 , 看到電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索利德運動的例子顯示 , 即使是小預算獨立電影也能扮演一個角色 , 把非暴力行為轉化成功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家所能擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始報導每週的非暴力示威 , 發生在像比爾的村落裡 , 尼恩 , 華納 , 在耶路撒冷 , 像席克•賈拉 , 和絲華──非暴力領袖在工作中會變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們就好像從來沒有發生過 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我看過第一手 , 如果我們這麼做 , 他們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們相乘 , 他們的影響力會在以色列的衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力 , 終於可以解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人已經證明了非暴力在布德鲁斯這類地方工作 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	讓我們給予他們注意力 , 讓他們可以證明它在各處都可行 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•史東克對於激勵人心的領導力有一個簡單但強而有力的模型 , 一切始於黃金圓圈 , 以及 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseyee , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導 , 領導 , 銷售 , 賣 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•史東克:偉大領袖如何啟發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	當事情不如我們假設時 , 該如何解釋 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更好的是 , 你要如何解釋 , 當其他人能夠成就似乎打敗所有假設時 , 要怎麼解釋 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們的比賽都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是個電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們只是和其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有相同的人才、同一個機構、同一個顧問、同一個媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼他們似乎有所不同呢 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國遭受預防權益的人 , 他肯定不是當時唯一偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出掌控的、有權力的男人飛行 , 肯定有其他隊伍更有資格 , 更有資格 。
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現人力飛行 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他玩耍的東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對我認為世界如何運作的看法 , 甚至深深地改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	事實證明 , 世界上所有偉大且激勵人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果或馬丁路德金 , 或萊特兄弟 , 他們都認為、行動、溝通都是一樣的 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且和其他人完全相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是把它編碼 , 可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼樣 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導者能夠激發其他人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們所做的 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們是怎麼辦到的 , 不論你稱之為你不同的價值主張或是你的財產過程或是你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或組織知道他們為什麼要做自己的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	藉由 " 為什麼 " 我不代表 " 來獲利 "
that's a result . it's always a result .	那是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	藉由 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	你的組織為什麼存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	你為什麼早上出床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果 , 我們的思考方式 , 我們採取行動的方式 , 我們的溝通方式來自外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這是顯而易見的 。 我們從最清楚的東西到最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但受到激勵的領導者和激勵的組織 , 不論它們的大小 , 不論它們的產業都認為 , 行動和溝通都來自內部 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果 , 因為它們很容易理解 , 大家都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果和其他人一樣 , 來自他們的行銷訊息可能會聽起來像這樣: 「 我們會製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	他們設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 」 「 嗯 。 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是大部分行銷的做法 , 大部分銷售都是這樣做的 , 也是我們大部分人交流的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何做得更好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師有最大客戶 , 我們總是為和我們一起做生意的客戶表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很棒的氣體哩程 , 它有皮座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	蘋果是這樣溝通的 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信思考的方式不同 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是 , 把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 用在友善的使用上 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是剛好製造出很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一個 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不同吧 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是 , 人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們會買你為什麼這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們會買你為什麼要做 。
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一個人都能完全自在地買一台蘋果電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很自在地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果手機 , 或蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能區別出他們在結構上和他們的競爭對手 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們嘗試了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出了平面的螢幕電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很有資格做出平面的螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	多年來他們都在做平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	迪爾帶著mp3播放器和pdas , 他們會製造出很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美設計的產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 說到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從dell買一個mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	你為什麼要從電腦公司購買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們會買你為什麼要做 。
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和需要你所擁有的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最好的部分是:沒有一個我告訴你的是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	全都在生物學的網絡中實現 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一個人腦的十字路口 , 從上下看 , 你看到的是人類的大腦實際上被分成三個主要的元件 , 與黃金圈完美相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 以 「 什麼 」 的層級來對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	新皮質負責我們所有的理性和分析性思維和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間的兩個部分組成了我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責我們所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外在溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內部溝通時 , 我們會直接和控制行為的腦部對話 , 然後我們讓人們用我們說的有形的東西將之合理化 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是腸道決策的來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你可以給某人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道所有事實和細節都說了什麼 , 但那就是感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用那個動詞 , 不是 「 感覺 」 的意思 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的大腦的部分無法控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最好能強調的是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時候你會說你帶著心去領導 , 或是帶著你的靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我討厭拆解它 , 那些不是其他身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你邊緣的腦部 , 控制決策的腦部 , 而不是語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼要做你的工作 , 人們會回應你為什麼做你所做的事 , 那你會如何讓別人為你投票 , 或向你買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 要忠誠 , 想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是賣給需要你的人 ; 目標是賣給那些相信你所相信的人 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的事的人 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人們只是因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 用血汗和淚水來幫你 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除了萊特兄弟之外 , 還有更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人都不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初期 , 追求有權力的人飛行就像是白天的網點com一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在試試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley我們假設是成功的食譜
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你問人們: 「 你的產品為什麼會失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	而人們總是給你相同的三件事:對錯、不對的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是一樣的三樣東西 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley被戰爭部門給予五萬美金來找出這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	金錢根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦一個座位 , 在史密森尼工作 , 非常聯結 ; 他知道當時所有的大型思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的心靈金錢可以找到 , 市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報到處跟著他 , 每一個人都在為langley著手 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼可能從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	在俄亥俄州的幾百哩外 , 奧維爾和威爾伯.萊特 , 他們沒有我們認為成功的秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們用自行車商店的收入來支付他們的夢想 ; 不是萊特兄弟的單一人有大學教育 , 甚至不是奧維爾或威爾布爾 ; 紐約時報到處跟蹤他們 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同之處在於 , 奧維爾和威爾堡是由一個理由 , 一個理由 , 一個理由 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能弄清楚這架飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley也不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 想成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	各位 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人和他們一起工作 , 帶著血汗、汗水和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只為支付費用 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是關於每次萊特兄弟出去時 , 他們就得拿五組零件 , 因為那是他們在來供應的前幾次車禍 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟搭飛機 , 甚至沒有人會去體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後我們發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley被錯誤的東西激勵著:萊特兄弟起飛的那天 , 他辭職了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說: 「 那是個了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你們的科技 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一位 , 他沒有變富有 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他就辭職了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們會買你為什麼要做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你所相信的人呢 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	某樣東西叫做 「 創新法則 」 , 如果你不知道 「 法律 」 , 你絕對知道 「 術語 」 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是你早期的多數人 , 已晚期的多數人和懶人 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到觸控式電話的唯一原因是你再也買不到輪手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在不同時間點上 , 但創新的擴散法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個點子 , 你就不能擁有它 , 直到達15%到18%的市場市場市場 , 系統的秘訣 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我很喜歡問企業: 「 你在新生意上轉換了什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約是10% , 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以超過百分之十的客人
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 拿到 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	那就像是那種直覺的感覺 , 「 喔 , 他們只是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到那些在你做生意之前得到的 , 而不是那些沒有得到它的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以 , 就是這個 , 你必須關閉的這個小缺口 , 如同jeffreymoore稱它為 「 跨越隔閡 」 , 因為 , 你看 , 早期的多數人不會嘗試什麼 , 直到別人先試過 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者和早期的採用者 , 他們很自在地做出那些直覺的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更能自在地做出那些直覺的決定 , 由他們所相信的世界所驅動 , 而不僅僅是那些產品能取得的東西 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊六小時來買iphone , 當他們第一次出櫃時 , 你可以在下週走進店裡 , 把一個買下來 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了四萬美金在平面電視上 , 當他們初次出櫃時 , 即使這項技術是後果的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便說一下 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術實在太棒了 , 他們自己也這麼做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想成為第一位
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不會買你做的事 ; 他們會買你為什麼做 , 以及你做的事 , 只能證明你所相信的事 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone的原因是前六小時 , 排隊排隊六小時 , 是因為他們相信世界 , 以及他們希望每個人都能看到他們:他們最初 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們會買你為什麼要做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及著名的創新法則的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	一個商業的例子
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說的 , 一秒鐘前 , 成功的食譜是金錢 , 正確的人 , 以及對的市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從約八九年前的提伏出來到現在 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手下 , 毫無疑問 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們極度富裕 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 ,
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我把東西綁在垃圾時間的華納dvr上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但是tivo是一個商業失敗的
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們去ipo時 , 他們的股票大約是三、四十美元 , 接著就跌倒了 , 從來沒有在十歲以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為這甚至在六歲以上交易 , 除了幾個小刺激之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一種能暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 讓現場現場電視 , 甚至不用你問 , 就記住你的觀看習慣 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們曾經說過: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你人生的每一面 , 男孩 , 我們是否有產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視 , 跳過商業廣告 , 記住你的觀看習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不會買你做什麼 ; 他們會買你為什麼要做 , 而你所做的只是作為你所相信的證明 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子 , 說明創新的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的商場上 , 聽見金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們送出沒有邀請函 , 也沒有網站查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	要怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是唯一一個在美國遭受前美國人民權益的男人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很差 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們美國需要改變什麼 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他走來走去告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的事的人 , 把他的成因 , 他們自己做出來 , 告訴別人 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中的一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個詞可以傳遞給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	此時此刻 , 有25萬人出現在對的時間 , 聽到他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為他出席 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出席 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們相信的美國 , 讓他們在公車上旅行了八小時 , 站在華盛頓的陽光下 , 在八月中間 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人對白人:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信世上有兩種法律:那些由高權威和那些由人類所製成的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類所制定的法律都與我們所制定的權威更高的法律一致 , 我們才會活在一個公正的世界裡 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正好發生在民權運動上 , 是幫助他為人生帶來理想上的完美之處 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽現在的政治人物 , 用他們全然的12點計劃 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有在鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 還有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的立場 , 但那些領導我們的人卻鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論他們是個人或組織 , 我們遵循那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 能夠激發他們周圍的人 , 或找到能激勵他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	要怎麼記得你把車停在哪裡 ? 要怎麼知道你是否往正確的方向移動 ? 神經學家尼爾•布魯奇研究我們周遭的空間繪製的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結到記憶和想像力 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦 , 認知科學 , 探索 , 神經科學 , 科學
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你身在何處
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場時 , 我們怎麼記得停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	面對荷馬的問題是:
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	並且我們會試著去了解他大腦裡發生的事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以 , 我們先從海馬體開始 , 用黃色表示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果那裡有損傷 , 就像在阿茲海默症中 , 你記不得的事情包括你把車停在哪裡 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它是以拉丁文為 「 海馬 」 的名字 , 它是它的組合 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人類的大腦裡大約有一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元會彼此溝通 , 藉由發送小脈衝或刺激的電流 , 互相連結 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體組成兩種細胞 , 非常密集地相互連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶如何運作 , 藉由在老鼠或老鼠身上的個別神經元記錄 , 來紀錄牠們覓食或探索一個尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們會想像 , 我們從這隻老鼠的海馬體中記錄下來 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出電流的刺激時 , 會有一個紅點和點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們看到 , 這種神經元知道 , 每當老鼠進入一個特定位置時 ,
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送一個小小的電流訊號到大腦的其他部位 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以把神經元的發射率顯示成動物所在位置的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中記錄 , 我們會發現 , 當動物進入環境中的不同部位時 , 不同的神經元會發射出 , 就像在這個方形盒子裡顯示的一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以 , 它們一起形成了大腦的其餘部分的地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時會需要他們大腦監測的電波活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	其中一些病人玩電玩遊戲 , 在那裡他們開車繞著一個小鎮
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	而在它們的嬉皮細胞會發射 , 變得活躍 , 每當它們開車經過一個特定位置時 , 就開始發送電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 一個位置細胞如何知道老鼠或人在其環境中的位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這裡的這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的界線特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 頂端的人喜歡在老鼠的牆壁之間打火 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你拓展盒子時 , 發射的位置會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面有一面牆壁接近南方 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 細胞就會在兩處都發射到南方 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 , 細胞就會發射到南方 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這預測了 , 感應周圍的距離和方向 , 延伸建築物的距離和方向 , 對海馬體來說是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在輸入海馬體的輸入中 , 細胞會被發現到海馬體中的哪些項目 , 它的確能以特定的距離來檢測界線或邊緣 , 在探究老鼠或老鼠的周圍時所做的反應 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 每當動物靠近一面牆或一條界線到東邊 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣或圓形的牆壁或圓形的圓形牆壁 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物都跑來跑去了 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞會發火 , 只要南邊有一條界線 , 不論是桌子的邊緣 , 或牆壁 , 或甚至兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 這是我們認為位置細胞的一種方式 , 決定動物在探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 例如這條目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看看他們必須記住的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放在他們認為旗幟或車子的位置 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和尺寸 , 就像我們用位置細胞做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟在哪裡被改變為你如何改變環境的形狀和尺寸 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你看到旗幟的位置在一個小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們它在哪裡 , 但你讓環境變大 , 他們認為旗幟的位置已經被伸展到完全相同的位置細胞會伸展出去 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記得旗幟在哪裡 , 藉由儲存你位置上所有的位置細胞的模式 , 然後你可以透過移動來回到那個位置 , 最好符合你儲存的位置細胞的目前模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那指引你回到你想要記住的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們透過運動來到哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 如果我們把一些外界的路徑 , 也許我們會停下來 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路的方向 , 大概就是要回去的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一個叫做 「 網格細胞 」 的細胞中取得這種通路整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在網格細胞再次被找到 , 輸入到海馬體 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個別的細胞都會在一系列的不同位置燃燒 , 這些位置會以驚人的三角形網格排出 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從幾個網格細胞中記錄下來 , 每個細胞在不同的顏色中都有一個類似網格的發射模式 , 每個細胞的網格狀圖案都和其他細胞有稍微的相對位置 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	這個格子上的紅色的火和綠色的在這個格子上是藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 一起來 , 就好像老鼠可以在它的環境中放置虛擬的電網 , 有點像是你在地圖上找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電流活動可以從其中一個細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 來追蹤它所在的位置 , 這樣它就能用它自己的移動來知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有類似網格的發射模式都有相同的對稱軸 , 相同的網格位置 , 在這裡以橘色表示 , 每個位置的網格細胞的淨活動 , 都應該根據我們是否沿著這六個方向行進 , 或沿著六個方向行進 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進磁共振掃描儀中 , 讓他們做個小小的電玩遊戲 , 像是我給你們看的 , 尋找這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人類的根部皮質中看到它 , 和你在老鼠身上看到網格細胞的同一個部分 。
so back to homer .	所以回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車在距離和方向的位置來延伸建築物和界限在他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	由邊界偵測細胞的發射所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他走出汽車公園的路徑 , 會在網格細胞的發射中呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	現在這兩種細胞都能使位置細胞發火 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以透過移動來回到他停車的地方 , 找到最適合位置的位置 , 來找到目前他大腦中儲存的位置細胞模式 , 讓他停車的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置 , 對視覺暗示的觀點 , 像是他的車子是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能已遭到困境 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 , 拿到它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整個大腦中尋找這種類似網格的發射模式 , 我們在一系列的位置 , 在我們做各式各樣的自傳記憶任務時 , 會一直活躍起來 , 比如 , 記得你上次去參加婚禮的時候 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 可能是 , 代表我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 也被用來產生視覺圖像 , 這樣我們才能在空間場景中重現 , 至少 , 在我們想象時發生的事件中 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以 , 如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從位置細胞開始 , 藉由這些密度的相互作用來啟動彼此 , 然後重新啟動邊界細胞 , 創造出你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以透過那個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部導向細胞 , 我還沒提到 , 它們會根據你面臨的方向 , 像羅盤一樣火 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你想要為你的視覺影像產生圖像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這個結婚時發生了什麼事 , 舉例來說 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個新時代的一個例子 , 存在於認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理的過程 , 像是你如何記得、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個個個別神經元的行為為基礎 , 來構成我們的大腦 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 全球安全由機構、政府、私營部門和公眾的合作驅動 。 這不只是開放原始碼粉絲的遙遠希望 , 也是詹姆斯•史塔維迪斯的願景 , 北托的最高指揮官 , 他分享了近期軍事歷史的生動時刻 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 應該用橋樑而不是牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•史塔維里迪斯:nato的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會談談開放式安全 , 因為在這21世紀 , 我們必須要在安全上變得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說一下 , 讓我們回顧二十世紀 , 有點像是 , 那種安全風格對我們如何工作 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個在法國的戰場 , 就在比利時的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在1916年的verdun , 在1916年 , 超過300天的時期 , 有70萬人死亡 , 所以一天大約2000人死亡 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它推向20世紀的安全性推進第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林格的戰役 , 300天 , 兩百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝戰變成第二次世界大戰的馬吉諾線 , 然後進入冷戰時期 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的論點是 , 與其建造牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	它是dra河的橋樑 , 是ivoandriic小說的主題 , 它談到如何 , 在歐洲和巴爾幹的那一塊非常麻煩的部分 , 經過一段時間 , 有著巨大的牆 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	更近期 , 在過去十年間 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫著 , 結合在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會再次辯論 , 開放式安全是要把國際、國際間、私人出版社連結起來 , 並將它與戰略性溝通大致在社交網絡中 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談我們為什麼需要這樣做 , 因為我們全球公有物以各種方式在攻擊 , 而沒有一個威脅到全球公有物的來源 , 將會透過建造牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個水手 , 很顯然 ,
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 一條線 , 穿過印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	上面有音樂廳的電線沿著它的側邊
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是防止海盜攻擊它 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	盜版是現今世界各地非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	盜版也在馬拉加的平台非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	活躍於幾內亞灣
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	它是全球運輸系統中10億美元的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 在這個時候 , 有20艘船 , 500個馬林人舉行人質 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何處理它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	來轉移到另一種海 , 網路海 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩位年輕男士的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	在當下 , 他們被監禁 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐欺 , 讓他們淨利超過一百億美元 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 它是全球經濟的2兆年不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	一年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	那只是在英國的大國內生產總值下面 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以 , 我們所知的這個網路大海是激進開放的基礎 , 也受到了威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我擔心全球公有物的另一件事 , 就是被販賣的威脅 , 被食品、鴉片的運動所影響 , 來自阿富汗 , 到美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心來自安地斯山脊北部的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器和人口販賣的運動 , 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販賣 , 以及它的糟糕成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要在海上移動 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你 , 這是我們海軍裝置的高科技片段 , 我們用它來阻止販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一種由毒品cartels所執行的半白化劑 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	是在南美的叢林裡建造的
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的木筏抓到它 , 它帶著六噸的古柯鹼 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	4號船員 。 精密的通訊號打掃了 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣 , 在毒品中 , 在人類身上 , 在武器上 , 上帝禁止 , 在大規模毀滅性武器中 , 是對全球公有物的威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	今天我們一起在阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一片花花田 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上80%到90%的花粉、鴉片和海洛因 , 從阿富汗出來 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到那裡 , 當然 , 恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的出發點 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的迫切性嵌在那裏 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以 , 這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 我們必須要處理的是什麼 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 在這裡 , 21世紀 ,
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們20世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們應該怎麼做 ?
